conducted in accordance with terms set forth in Attachment A, all of 
which are incorporated into this Letter of Agreement by reference 
and binding on the parties hereto.  
  
7. Nothing contained in this Letter  of Agreement or in Section 1, Scope, of the

obligation on the part of the corporate parent of Northern Aviation Services, 
Inc., to recognize the Union  as an exclusive bargaining agent or otherwise

applicable law.

in all respects to be subject to the terms and conditions of subsection 1.H  
and Section 20.

RE: SCOPE 1 -002 
This Letter Of Agreement (“LOA”) is made and entered into in accordance with the 
provisions of the Railway Labor Act, as amended (“RLA”), by and between 
Northern Air Cargo (“NAC” or “the Company”), Aeko Kula dba Aloha Air Cargo 
(“Aloha Air Cargo”), their successors and assigns, and their Parent, Northern 
Aviation Services, its successors and assigns, and the Pilots in the service of the 
Company, as represented by the International Brotherhood Of Teamsters, Airline 
Division (“IBT” or  “the Union”).  
WHEREAS, the parties wish to avoid any disputes over the Company’s obligations 
under the IBT -Northern Air Cargo Agreement (“CBA”) pending the sale, transfer, 
conveyance or surrender of Aloha Air Cargo’s operating certificate;  
NOW, THEREFO RE, the parties agree and  stipulate as follows:  
A.On or before the date of the Aeko Kula operating certificate is sold, transferred,
conveyed or surrendered, or May 1, 2019, whichever occurs first, 1) Pilots
employed by Aloha Air Cargo shall be employed by Northern Air Cargo; 2) al l
aircraft Assigned to the Aeko Kula  operating certificate will be transferred to the
Northern Air Cargo operating certificate; and 3) all operations under the Aeko
Kula operating certificate by the signatories to this Letter of Ag reement and
their Affilia tes shall cease. The parties may extend the May 1, 2019 date by
mutual agreement.  Flying by or on behalf of the Entity to which the former Aeko
Kula operating certificate is sold, transferred or conveyed shall not (1) cause
the Furlough or prevent the Recall  of Pilots, (2) reduce the compensation orDocuSign Envelope ID: 7A46D395-CB86-4F80-B6A9-EE3300CB9708
Page 295 of 333

--- PAGE BREAK ---

benefits of Pilots; (3) reduce the number of pilots in any Position; or (4) slow 
the growth of the craft or class of Pilots.  
B.The Aeko Kula  operating certificate shall not be sold, transferred, conveyed or
transferred to an Affiliate as that term is defined in Section 1 of the CBA.
C.On the date of the sale, transfer, conveyance or surrender, or May 1, 2019
(unless the parties agree to an extension), whichever occurs first, Aeko Kula
shall cease to exist as an Entity as the term is defined in Section 1 of the CBA.
However, it shall not be a violation of this Letter of Agreement or the CBA if
Aloha Air Cargo remains an Affiliate of Northern Aviation Services  operating
exclusively as a n indirect carrier; provided, all freight transported by air on
behalf of Aloha Air Cargo and/or its customers shall be performed by Pilots on
the Northern Air Cargo Integrated Seniority List (ISL) in accordance with the
CBA.
D.Except as set forth in this LOA,  the terms of the CBA apply to Pilots employed
by Aloha Air Cargo and/or Assigned to aircraft on the operating certificate of
Aeko Kula, including all of the terms of Section 1 of the CBA and associated
letters of agreement, without distinction between  Pilots employed by Northern
Air Cargo and Pilots employed by Aloha Air Cargo. Without limiting the
aforementioned statement, Section 1.F and 1.G, and all of the rights and
obligations contained therein, apply to all Pilots on the ISL regardless of the
carrier that employs the Pilots.
E.The existence of Aeko Kula, the continuing Assignment  of designated B737
aircraft to the Aeko Kula operating certificate, and the Assignment  of Pilots on
the ISL to operate such aircraft, shall not be treated as a violation  of Section 1
of the CBA, pending the sale, transfer, conveyance or surrender of the Aeko
Kula operating certificate or until May 1, 2019, whichever occurs first; provided:
1.Without limiting the terms of Paragraph D above, Pilots may bid and be
awarded Vac ancies (including displacements) on the Northern Air Cargo
operating certificate or Aeko Kula operating certificate in accordance with
Section 18, regardless of the carrier that employs the Pilot during the period
referred to in Paragraph E above.
2.Only B 737 aircraft with registration numbers 301 KH, 302 KH, 303 KH and
361 NC may be Assigned to the Aeko Kula operating certificate during the
above -referenced period.
F.This LOA shall become effective upon signing and shall remain in full force and
effect in acco rdance with the terms of Section 32 of the CBA, except as limited
by its terms and unless terminated sooner by mutual agreement of the parties;
provided , it may be amended by mutual agreement of the parties at any time.DocuSign Envelope ID: 7A46D395-CB86-4F80-B6A9-EE3300CB9708

This Letter of Agreement (“LOA”) is made and entered into in accordance with the

increased f lying opportunities resulting from the acquisition of Strat  Air should be 
allocated in a manner that is responsive to the needs of the business for the benefit 
of all stakeholders;

be performed by Pilots on the Northern Air Cargo Seniority List in
accordance with Section 1 of the IBT -Northern Air Cargo Agreement (CBA)

2.Nothing contained in this LOA shall modify the specific exceptions to
Section 1.D or the Wet Lease provisions set forth in  Section 1.E of the CBA,

or similar aircraft with an MTOW of 139,500 lbs. or less operated by Swift
Air (or another carrier in lieu of Swift Air) in  MIA, to perform ad

pairs served by Swift Air (MIA -KIN, KIN -MBJ, MBJ -MIA, MIA -GEO, GEO -
PBM , PBM -MIA, MIA -BGI, BGI -POS, POS -MIA, POS -GEO, GEO -PBM,

following conditions:
a.Revenue flying under the Wet Lease in support of Strat  Air cannot
exceed an average of one hundred and fifty (150) hours per Month
(based on a rolling six (6) Month period);
(1) The Company shall provide  the Union with the aircraft registration
number of the aircraft referred to in this Paragraph 3.
(2) The Company shall provide the Union with hourly flight data on a
Monthly basis in a form acceptable to the Union.
(3) If the average one hundred and fifty (150) hours per Month limit is
exceeded, the right to Wet Lease under this Paragraph 3 shall be
null and void sixty (60) Days  thereafter unless the parties mutually
agree otherwise.
b.A Wet Lease under this LOA shall not: (1) cause the Furlough or prevent
the Recall of Pilots, (2) reduce the compensation or benefits of Pilots;
(3) reduce the number of Pilots in any Position; or (4) slow the growth of
the craft or class of Pilots; and
c. Section 1.E.2 of the CBA shall be inapplicable to flying in support of Str at
Air operations if the Company invokes Paragraph 3 of this LOA, except
the Company shall not be precluded from entering into a Wet Lease for
a New Market as provided in Section 1.E.2.
4.This LOA shall become ef fective upon signing and shall remain in fu ll force
and effect in accordance with the terms of Section 32 of the CBA unless
earlier terminated by mutual agreement of the parties; provided , it may be
amended by mutual agreement of the parties at any time.

This LETTER OF AGREEM ENT (“LOA”) is made and entered into in ac cordance

the craft or class of Pilots” as set forth in Section 1 of the Agreement and

WHEREAS, the parties are committed to attempting to resolve related disputes 
through good faith discussions based on empirical data;

1.

thereafter (“B767 Fence Period 2”), the Company shall award the first nine

Re: Flight  Pay Loss 
THIS LETTER OF AGREEMENT (LOA)  is made and entered into in accordance 
with the provisions of Title II of the Railway Labor Act, as amended, by and 
between Northern Air Cargo, Inc. (the “Company”) and the International 
Brotherhood of  Teamsters, Airline Division, as administratively delegated to 
Teamsters Local 959 (the “Union”), hereinafter known as the “Parties”.  
WHEREAS, the administration of the Collective Bargaining Agreement 
("Agreement"), the performance of Union duties related to the representation of 
Pilots, the Parties’ mutual interest in avoiding undue disruption of Company 
operations, and ongoing labor -management cooperation requires the release of 
Pilots from conflicting Duty; and  
WHEREAS, the parties have agreed upon procedures related to flight pay loss 
and benefit reimbur sement related to the release of flight Pilots who perform 
Union duties.  
NOW, THEREFORE, the Parties agree as follows:  DocuSign Envelope ID: 7A46D395-CB86-4F80-B6A9-EE3300CB9708
Page 309 of 333

--- PAGE BREAK ---

1.When the Union wishes that a Pilot be released from Duty for Union
business, the Union shall present a written request to the Company
identifying the Pilots to be released and the release dates including travel
Days.  Requests for release from Duty for Union Leave and Company
responsibilities for assuring that a Pilot is available to  perform Union duties
hall be made, as provided Section 8 (Leaves of Absence).
2.The Company shall pay “Flight Pay Loss” (FPL) to a Pilot for all Duty
which he or she is released from to participate in approved Union
business.  FPL shall include the scheduled PCH of the Duty Assignment
for which the Pilo t is removed for Union Leave, plus a 12.65% override to
cover his 401K contribution, FICA, Medicare and State Unemployment.
Duty time covered by FPL payments shall be included within a Pilot’s
earnings  for the pay period in which the FPL was incurred.  Up on request
from the Union, the Company shall submit the monthly Crew Time
Reports, which verifies the scheduled Credit Pay for each Duty
Assignment lost due to his Union activity.
3.As provided in paragraph 2 above, at the start of the Pilot Define
Contribu tion Plan on July 1, 2021, the override percentage to cover a
Pilot’s Define Contribution and 401K contributions, FICA, Medicare and
State Unemployment shall be increased to 16.25%.
4.With the exception set out in paragraph 6 below, the Union shall
reimburs e the Company for FPL paid to a Pilot who has been released for
Union business.  The Company shall provide an itemized bill to the Union
within forty -five (45) Days of the last Day of the Bid Period in which the
Pilot was paid F PL for Union business.  The billing statement shall include,
separately for each Pilot, the Pilot’s name, dates and reimbursement
calculation, based upon the Pilot’s hourly pay rate, as provided for in
Attachment A of the Agreemen t and, on a per -Day basis, the Pilot’s
scheduled Duty hours from which he or she was released.   The Union
shall issue payment to the Company within thirty (30) Days of receipt of
the Company’s billing statement.
5.The Union shall not be required to reimb urse the Company for FPL or any
additional compensation paid to a Pilot for participation in the Event
Review Committee (ERC) under ASAP, for acting as a “Gatekeeper”DocuSign Envelope ID: 7A46D395-CB86-4F80-B6A9-EE3300CB9708
Page 310 of 333

--- PAGE BREAK ---

under FOQA, or any other meetings  required by the  Company , as 
provided for in th e Agreeme nt.  
6.It is mutually understood by the parties that th e Agreement provides for a
Monthly period for pay purposes. For the purposes of this LOA, as it
relates to a Pilot’s pay period, the term “Month” shall be used.
7.As provided in Section 8 (Leaves of Absence), a Pilot shall continue to
accrue Seniority and Longevity while released for Union Leave.  No
deduction from a Pilot’s Seniority or Longevity shall be made when
released for Union Leave.

RE: B767 RETROACTIVE PAY (RETRO PAY)  
THIS LETTER OF AGREEMENT  (LOA)  is made and entered into in accordance 
with the provisions of the Railway Labor Act, as amended, by and between 
Northern Air Cargo, Inc. (“Northern Air Cargo” or the “Company”) and the 
International Brotherhood of Teamsters (“IBT” or the “Union”).  
WHEREAS, the parties have agreed that the B767  Pilots shall receive 
Retroactive Pay (Retro Pay), from the date each individual Pilot flew his first 
Operating Experience (OE) Flight Assignment for the Company as a 
Crewmember in the B767 (Active B767 Pilot), up to the Date of Signing (DOS) of 
the Agreem ent; 
WHEREAS, the parties agree that prior to this LOA the Company utilized Active 
B767 Pilots from both Northern  Air Cargo (NAC) and Aloha Air Cargo (AAC), who 
were working under their separate Collective Bargaining Agreements (CBA’s) 
and except as otherwise provided for in this L OA, it is understood that different  
Hourly Pay Rate s and contractual  provisions  which are to be  applied when 
calculating each individual Active B767 Pilot’s Retro Pay.  
NOW THEREFORE, the parties hereby agree as follows:  
1. Retro Pay at the DOS of th e Agreement.
The Company shall pay Retro Pay to each individual Active B767 Pilot in
connection with the DOS of th is LOA . The Retro Pay shall be  based on the
differences in the Hourly Pay Rate, as provided in paragraph two (2) below ,DocuSign Envelope ID: 7A46D395-CB86-4F80-B6A9-EE3300CB9708
Page 312 of 333

--- PAGE BREAK ---

including any differences  in fringe benefits or other payments that were legally 
or contractually required to be made (e.g., 401(k) retirement contributions, 
social security, payroll taxes)  for compensation received  prior to the DOS of 
the Agreement.  
2. An Active B767 Pilot’s Individual Retro Pay Amount shall be equal to his
Hourly Pay Rate Differential (His applicable B767 Hourly Pay Rate, as
provided in Appendix A of Section 3, Compensation minus the Hourly Pay
Rate  that he was paid prior to the DOS  of this LOA ) multiplied by the total
amount of Credit Pay or Pay Credit Hours (PCH), whichever is applicable,
that he earned as an Active B767 Pilot prior to the DOS of th e Agreement .
3.All applicable Hourly Pay Rates an Active B767 Pilot’s earnings were paid at
prior to the DOS of th e Agreement shall be used in his Retro Pay calculation.
4.The Company shall provide all relevant Pilot data and information to the
Union in connection with the calculation of each individual Active B767 Pilot’s
Retro Pay, including the entire list of Active B767 Pilots, prior to the DOS of
this LOA. The Company shal l provide any additional data or information that
is reasonably requested by the Union.
5.Any dispute between the Company and the Union concerning interpretation or
application of this L OA shall be subject to the Expedited Dispute Resolution
procedures,  as provided in subsection 1.H. of the Agreement.
6.The Company shall provide the Union with all relevant data and Information,
as provided in paragraph four (4), within fourteen (14) Days after the DOS of
the Agreement .
7.The “Payment Date” for Activ e B767 Pilots Retro Pay shall occur no later than
thirty (30) Days after the DOS of the Agreement .
8.All potential disputes involving Active B767 Pilots Retro Pay shall be
submitted by the Union to the Director of Operations, or his designee within
thirty (30) Days after the Payment Date.
This LOA shall become effective on the DOS of the Agreement between the 
Company and the Union and shall remain in full force and effect concurrent with 
the Agreement.

RE: SECTION 2, DEFINITIONS, SECTION 3.S., INSTRUCTO R PILOT, CHECK AIRMAN AND

INCLUDE DOMICILE FLEX LINES AND TRIP DROP PROVISION S 
 
 
THIS LETTER OF AGREEMENT is made and entered into i n accordance with the provisions of 
the Railway Labor Act, as amended, by and between N ORTHERN AIR CARGO, INC (the 
“Company”) and the INTERNATIONAL BROTHERHOOD OF TEA MSTERS (the “Union”).  
 
WHEREAS additions to Section 2, Definitions are requ ired for newly created terminology; and 
 
WHEREAS the parties, recognize the need to fairly co mpensate Instructors, Check Airmen and 
Aircrew Program Designees (APD’s) commensurate with  their additional obligations and 
responsibilities, as provided in subsection 3.S.; a nd 
 
WHEREAS the parties wish to improve Line Constructio n options for the Pilots with the creation 
of Domicile Flex Lines; and 
 
WHEREAS the parties wish to create a more defined structure that provides bett er guidance when 
the Company is determining whether to “approve” or “deny” a Trip D rop request from a Pilot, as 
provided in subsection 14.M; and 
 
WHERAS the parties agree that the provisions contain ed in this Letter of Agreement (LOA) shall 
supersede the previous existing provisions in subse ctions 3.S.,14.D., 14.E. and 14.M. of this 
Agreement. 
 
NOW, THEREFORE, it is mutually agreed that: 

--- PAGE BREAK ---

SECTION 2 
DEFINITIONS 
 
A Ghost Bid A Line that a Full-Time Check Airman or Instructor Pil ot has bid for, 
and as a result of his ineligibility to bid for that Mont h, as provided in 
subsection 14.C., he shall not be awarded a Line that wo uld have 
been awarded had it not been for his Full-Time Check Airman or 
Instructor status for that Month, but through such Ghost Bid, he shall 
retain such Initial Line’s  PCH for the purpose of establishing his new 
MPG for that Month. All Ghost Bids shall be awarded in Seniori ty 
Order, in relation to his Position in his Domicile. 

--- PAGE BREAK ---

SECTION 3 
COMPENSATION 
 
S. AIRCREW PROGRAM DESIGNEE, CHECK AIRMAN AND INSTRUCTOR PILOT 
PREMIUMS 
 
1. All Line Check Airman (LCA) and/or Simulator Check Airman (SCA), to includ e 
Aircrew Program Designee(s) (APD’s) and Check Airman performing ground 
school instruction, in addition to Section 3, Compensatio n, shall receive the 
following premiums; 
 
a. All Check Airman shall receive a monthly override of 10% for all cumulative 
PCH in a Monthly Bid Period. 
 
b. An APD shall receive an override of $75.00 per hour above his adjusted 
Check Airman hourly pay rate as provided in Section 3.S.1.a., fo r all training 
and checking events while serving in the capacity of an APD. 
 
c. All Check Airman shall receive an override of $50.00 per hour abo ve his 
adjusted Check Airman hourly pay rate as provided in Section 3.S. 1.a., for 
all training, checking, simulator, ground school and briefing events when 
acting in the capacity of a Check Airman. 
 
d. Check Airman performing administrative duties at the direction of the Training 
Department shall be credited for such duty as provided for in Section 3.S.1.a. 
 
e. The minimum PCH for a Check Airman performing an Assignment shall not  
be less than the DPG. 
 
2. Simulator and/or Ground School instructors, in addition to Sectio n 3, 
Compensation, shall receive the following premiums; 
 
a. A simulator and/or ground school instructor performing simulator or ground 
school training event(s), shall receive an override of $35.00  per hour above 
his hourly pay rate as provided in Section 3, Appendix A, Comp ensation. 
 
b. A Simulator and/or Ground School Instructor shall receive a 10% ho urly 
override on a Day-by-Day basis, for any administrative duty performed at the 
direction of the Training Department. 
 
c. The minimum PCH for a Simulator or Ground School Instructor shall n ot be 
less than the DPG. 
 
3. Ghost Bids 

--- PAGE BREAK ---

a. When a Check Airman is unable to bid for a Line, as provide d in Section 
14.C.4.b.(4)., he shall be afforded the opportunity to “Ghost  Bid” for a Line of 
Flying during the Initial Line Bid Period, as provided in subsections 14.C.6 or 
14.C.7. A Pilot who Ghost Bids shall not be awarded a Line  during the Initial 
Line Bid Period. 
 
b. The Ghost Bid Award shall become a Pilot’s new MPG for the  Month. 
 
c. As provided in subsection 3.S.3.b., his new MPG, as the result of  his Ghost 
Bid, shall be use d when calculating a Check Airman’s Monthly Cumulative 
PCH, as provided in subsection 3.N. 
 
d. A Check Airman shall be paid for all Premiums and additional PCH earned 
during the Month above his new MPG, resulting from his Ghost Bi d, as 
provided for in Section 3 (Compensation). 
 
e. A Check Airman or Instructor Pilot who Ghost Bids shall be available  to be 
scheduled by the Training Department to perform Training Duti es, as 
provided in Section 22.D. 
 
4. General 
 
a. When an Instructor, Check Airman or APD is Assigned to perform Trainin g 
on a lesser-paid Aircraft Type, he shall receive the applicabl e Hourly Pay 
Rate for the Position his system-wide Seniority allows him to h old for all 
earned PCH in the Month, provided he bids for and is award ed a Vacancy 
(“Phantom Award”) in the higher paying  Position. 
 
b. A Check Airman performing an Assignment on a scheduled Day Off, he shall 
be paid one hundred and fifty percent (150%) of his appli cable Hourly Pay 
Rate in addition to the provisions  provided in Section 3.S. 1 and 3.S.2.  
Such compensation shall be paid in addition to all PCH accumu lated during 
a Month, as provided in subsection 3.N. 
 
5. Flight Operations shall consider current Check Airman recommendation s when 
selecting new Check Airman or Instructors during the respective Vaca ncy 
Process.

SECTION 14 
SCHEDULING 
 
D. TRIP PAIRING CONSTRUCTION 
 
1. A Trip Pairing shall consist of one (1) or more Duty Periods and co ntain any 
mixture of Flight and/or Deadhead Segments, and under limit ed circumstances 
R-1 or R-2 RAPs, as provided for in this subsection 14.D. 
 
2. The Company shall construct, to the greatest extent possible, Trip Pairings in the 
following order of prioritization: 
 
a. The maximum number of Trip Pairings with Flight Segments and /or 
Deadhead Segments, then, 
 
b. Trip Pairings with Reserve Assignments and/or Split-Trip Pairings, as 
provided in 14.D.3. 
 
3. Trip Pairings shall be constructed utilizing all “Known Flying” at the 
commencement of each Month’s In itial Line Bid Period as provided in Section 
14.C.6. Known Flying shall be defined as all Flight Segm ents known to be 
performed by the Company prior to the commencement of each Monthl y Initial 
Line Bid Period. When the Company has been contracted to perf orm Charters, 
Ad-Hoc or ACMI contracts, all such Flying shall also be included in that Month’s 
Known Flying. No less than five (5) Days prior to the commencement  of each 
Initial Line Bid Period, the Company shall provide the JSC  with a list of all Known 
Flying, their initial draft of Trip Pairings and Lines for e ach Position, in all 
Domiciles. 
 
4. For Flight Segments or RAP’s  that originate and/or end at a location other than a 
Pilot’s Domicile, the Company shall schedule Deadhead segme nts on the front  
and back end of such Trip Pairings in order to reposition the Pilot from his 
Domicile or his Primary Residence if on an R3, to and from such Out- of-Domicile 
location. The Company shall schedule all such Deadhead segme nts in a Trip 
Pairing as far in advance as possible. 
 
5. If during Trip Pairing construction, as provided in subsection 1 4.D.2., the 
Company has an additional need for Reserve staffing in a spe cific Position in a 
Domicile; or the PCH of a Trip Pairing is less than the DPG, t hey may construct 
a Split-Trip Pairing utilizing Known Flying Flight Segments, or a modified R-1 or 
R-2 Reserve Assignment. Such Split-Trip Pairings may be constructed an d may 
be used to assist in meeting the Regular Line construction req uirements, as 
provided in subsection 14.E.5. Split Trips shall be constructed a s follows: 
 
a. Trip Pairings with R-1 RAPs, Trip Pairings and Deadhead Segments when 
the RAP is scheduled to be performed in a Company designated  Domicile. 

--- PAGE BREAK ---

 
b. Trip Pairings with R-2 RAPs, Trip Pairings and Deadhead Segments when 
the R-2 RAP is scheduled to be performed at a location other than a Domicile. 
 
6. If an R1 or R2 RAP follows the last Flight and/or Deadhea d Segment in a single 
Duty Period and a Pilot has not received another Duty Assignment within one (1) 
hour after Block- In of his previous Assignment in that same Duty Period, he shall 
be released from the remaining portion of his scheduled Duty and paid for all Duty 
he performed and for the scheduled Duty that was dropped due  to such release, 
as provided in Section 3 (Compensation). 
 
7. Trip Pairing construction may also contain Deadhead Segments a nd Reserve 
Availability Periods (RAP’s).  After the start of each Month’s  Initial Line Bid Period 
any new Flight Segments that becomes Known Flying shall be constructed into a 
Trip Pairing(s) and the subsequently put into Open Time or Assig ned to a 
Reserve Pilot as provided for in this Agreement. 
 
8. The maximum duration of a single Trip Pairing that originat es and ends in the 
same Month shall not exceed seventeen (17) consecutive Days (inclu sive of all 
scheduled Rest Periods within such Trip Pairing) when constructe d into an Initial 
Line.  
 
9. The maximum duration of a single Trip Pairing that originate s in one Month and 
ends in the following Month (inclusive of all scheduled Re st Periods), , shall not 
exceed more than twenty (20) consecutive Days and shall abide b y the 
provisions, as provided for in this Section 14.E.2.c., and 14. E.2.d. when 
constructed into an Initial Line. 
 
1 0.  The maximum duration of a single Trip Pairing in a TDY Line t hat originates and 
ends in the same Month shall not exceed eighteen (18) Days (in clusive of all 
scheduled Rest Periods), when constructed into an Initial Lin e. 
 
1 1.   The maximum duration of a single Trip Pairing in a TDY Line t hat originates in 
one Month and ends in the following Month (inclusive of a ll scheduled Rest 
Periods), , shall not exceed more than twenty (20) consecutive Days and shall 
abide by the provisions as provided for in this Section 14.E. 2.c., and 14.E.2.d. 
when constructed into an Initial Line. 
 
1 2.   All other Trip Pairings that are constructed after the publi shing of the Initial Lines 
shall follow the same maximum duration limitations, as provided  for in 
subsections 14.D.8., 14.D.9, 14.D.10. and 14.D.11. 
 
1 3.  The portion of a Trip Pairing, as provided for in subsections 14.D.9 and 14.D.11., 
that “transitions” into the following Month, shall be int egrated, as provided in 
subsection 14.F.5 (Month-End Integration. 

--- PAGE BREAK ---

E. MONTHLY LINE OF FLYING CONSTRUCTION PARAMETERS 
 
1. The published Initial Lines shall be constructed as Regular, Reserve, Composite 
and Domicile Flex Lines, as provided for in this subsection 1 4.E. Except as 
otherwise provided in this Section 14, all Lines shall be  bid for and awarded in 
Seniority Order, in each Position, per Domicile. Each Position and Domicile shall 
utilize either the Primary or Secondary Bid Process, as authorized by the JSC. 
 
2. The prioritization for constructing Initial Lines, in the f ollowing sequential order, 
shall be administered each Month when constructing all Line s for each Position 
in a Domicile: 
 
a. The total number of constructed Initial Lines, Including Do micile Flex Lines, 
shall equal and not exceed the number of its bidding Pilo ts in each Position 
at a Domicile for that Month. 
 
b. All Regular, Composite, Reserve and Domicile Flex Lines shal l have at least 
two (2) separate periods of at least three (3) consecutive Days Off or a single 
block of at least five (5) consecutive Days Off. 
 
c. All published Initial Lines (i.e. Regular, Composite, R eserve, or Domicile Flex 
Lines) during the Monthly Bid Period shall be constructed wi th no more than 
seventeen (17) scheduled Workdays in any given Month (including all 
scheduled Duty and/or other Company-Directed Assignments). 
 
d. The Minimum scheduled Days Off in all constructed Initial Line s shall be 
thirteen (13) Days Off for a thirty (30) Day Month and fourteen (14) Days Off 
in thirty-one (31) Day Month. 
 
e. All scheduled Days Off in the published Initial and Final Line awards shall b e 
scheduled in the Pilot’s  Domicile. 
 
f. All Initial Lines shall be constructed to be no greater than  ninety-five (95) 
PCH. Any Trip Pairings not constructed in a Line shall be placed into in Open 
Time. 
 
g. Regular Lines shall be constructed first with Trips from all of the Month’s 
Known Flying. 
 
(1) The Company shall, to the maximum extent possible construct Trip 
Pairings with the highest PCH into Regular Lines and holdb ack Trip 
Pairings with a lesser PCH value in Open Time, however, the C ompany 
shall not be restricted from optimizing Regular Line Constructio n by 
substituting or adding the minimum number of lower PCH Trip Pai rings 
for higher PCH Trip Pairings to maximize the number of Regular L ines 
constructed. 

--- PAGE BREAK ---

 
(2) The Company shall build the maximum number of Regular Lines, without 
any Reserve Assignments, for each Initial Line Bid Period. 
 
(3) Once such “pure” Regular Lines cannot be constructed, the Company  
may then continue to build Regular Lines with Trip Pairings to include 
Reserve Assignments as provided in subsection 14.E.5.a. 
 
h. When constructing Regular Lines, the lowest numbered publi shed Line shall 
be constructed with the maximum PCH. The following lowest n umbered 
Regular Line shall be constructed with the same or less PCH as the previous 
Line. This shall continue in this sequence until the last  Regular Line 
constructed that results in reducing the Trip Pairing PCH for tha t specific 
Position and Domicile to a level at least below  fifteen percent (15%) PCH, but 
greater than three percent (3%) of such total PCH. 
 
i. Once the Initial phase of the Regular Lines has conclud ed, the required 
Composite and Reserve Lines, as provided in this Section 14,  shall be 
constructed. In the event there is an inadequate number of Pilots to build the 
required number of Reserve and/or Composite Lines in a Positio n at a 
Domicile, the Company may construct R2 Reserve Lines  in another Domicile 
to supplement temporary staffing deficits in such Domicile. In a ll cases, 
Composite Line construction shall supersede Reserve Line constru ction and 
Regular Line construction shall supersede both Composite an d Reserve Line 
construction. 
 
j. If three (3) or more Reserve Lines are constructed and there are P ilots 
requesting to bid for Domicile Flex Lines, fifty percent (50% ) of the Reserve 
Lines, rounded up to the nearest whole integer, shall be  constructed as 
Domicile Flex Lines for those pilots requesting a Domicile Fl ex Line. 
 
k. Once it is determined how many Domicile Flex Lines shall be pu blished and 
if additional Lines that can be built utilizing the con struction parameters in 
subsection 14.E.6., the Company, in consultation with the JSC , sha ll 
construct additional Regular and/or Reserve Lines until no ot her Lines can 
be constructed. When additional Reserve Lines are created and  if there are 
additional Pilots who are requesting to bid for Domicile Flex Lines, such Lines 
shall be constructed using the ratio as provided for in this subsection 14.E.2.j. 
 
3. All TDY Lines shall be constructed as other Lines, with the fo llowing exceptions: 
 
a. All Trip Pairings in a TDY Line,  shall be scheduled to originate and end at the 
TDY Location, except for Trip Pairings to and from his Domicile and a TDY 
Location. 

--- PAGE BREAK ---

b. When Reserve Duty Periods are constructed in a TDY Line, they shall Duty 
On and Duty Off at the TDY Location, except as provided el sewhere in this 
Section 14. 
 
c. All published TDY Lines during the Monthly Bid Period shall be constructed 
with no more than eighteen (18) scheduled Workdays in a Month inclusive of 
any Deadhead between a Pilot’s Primary Residence and the lo cation(s) 
where his TDY Assignment is scheduled to originate and/or end . 
 
d. For all TDY Lines, the minimum Days Off requirement shall be t welve (12) 
Days Off in a thirty (30) Day Month and thirteen (13) Days Off in a thirty-one 
Day Month. 
 
e. At least fifty percent (50%) of TDY Lines  shall be scheduled to begin  and end 
in the same Mo nth. The remaining TDY Lines may be scheduled to “carry 
over” into the subsequent Month.  
 
f. Scheduled Days Off within a block of Workdays at a TDY Locat ion shall not 
be considered a Day Off for the purposes of meeting the Pil ot’s Minimum 
Days Off in Domicile requirement. 
 
4. All published Initial Lines that are constructed and award ed during the Initial Bid 
Period, and except as provided for in Section 8 (Leaves of Absence ), all Final 
Awarded and Assigned Lines at the conclusion of the Monthly Bid Period, shall 
be valued at no less than MPG, as provided in Section 3 (Compen sation). 
 
5. Regular Lines 
 
a. A Regular Line is a planned sequence created solely of Trip Pairings in a 
Month, except when maximizing the number of Regular Lines in  a Position 
and Domicile, as provided for in subsections 14.E.2.g. The maxim um 
number of R- 1 RAP’s in any given Regular Line shall not exceed six  (6). 
 
b. Regular Lines shall be constructed and published during the Initial Line Bid 
Period, as provided in subsections 14.C.6. and/or 14.C.7. an d this 14.E. 
 
c. A Regular Line shall be constructed with at least one (1) sche duled Day Off 
in any seven (7) consecutive Days. 
 
d. To the maximum extent possible, per Position and Domicile, th e Company 
shall construct Regular Lines with blocks of Workdays that are sched uled 
with consistent Weekly work patterns and Report Times (e.g., W orkdays 
scheduled on Sunday through Thursday each Week, or as close to a  weekly 
Workday pattern, all AM or PM DOT’s for scheduled Assignments) 
throughout the Month. This provision shall not be utilized if doing so would 

--- PAGE BREAK ---

prohibit the Company from adhering to the other provisions in this subsectio n 
14.E. 
 
e. To the maximum extent possible, a Regular Line shall not be constructed 
with single Days Off during the Month, except for the first or the last Day of 
the Month. When this limitation cannot be avoided, due t o the inability to 
construct a Regular Line to the MPG, a Regular  Line may be constructed with 
the minimum number of scheduled single Days Off in a Month in  order to 
achieve such requirement. 
 
f. All Trip Pairings in a Regular Line shall be scheduled to begin  and end at the 
Pilot’s Domicile. In the event of a TDY Vacancy Award, it may be eithe r his 
Domicile or Residence Airport, as defined in Section 15.B.4. c., Reserves. 
Once he is in his TDY Location, all subsequent Trip Pairings sh all begin and 
end in that location. 
 
g. R-3 Reserve Assignments shall not be scheduled onto Regular Lines.  
 
h. To the maximum Extent Possible, the Company shall schedule all Ni ght Trip 
Pairings consecutively when they are constructed into a Regular Line. 
 
i. In-Domicile: 
 
(1) No more than four (4) consecutive Night Trip Pairings in- Domici le shall 
be scheduled in a row without at least two (2) consecutive Sche duled 
Days Off. 
 
(2) A Night Trip Pairing that originates and ends in-Domicile sha ll not be 
scheduled to Duty Off the Day before the following sched uled Night Trip 
Pairing’s DOT in his Line, nor shall a Night Trip Pairing’s D OT be 
scheduled the Day after the previous Night  Trip Pairing’s  scheduled Duty 
Off Time (“no  staggering”).  
 
j. Out-of-Domicile: 
 
(1) When constructing Multi-day Trip Pairings out-of-Domicile, to include 
Ferry Flight or Deadhead Segments, the Company shall, to the  best of 
their ability, not stagger Night Flight Assignments within a  Trip Pairing 
(“no staggering”).  
 
(2) Multi-day Trip Pairings Out- of-Domicile, to include Ferry Flight or 
Deadhead Segments, shall not be scheduled for more than 4 
consecutive Night Trip Pairing Assignments. A minimum of two (2) 
consecutive Days of Reserve Assignments shall follow any 4 consecutive 
Night  Trip Assignments. During such two Days of Reserve Assignments, 
the Company shall be responsible for scheduling a continuous twenty- 

--- PAGE BREAK ---

four (24) hour Rest Period for such Pilot, free from all Duty, bef ore he is 
required to perform his next Duty Assignment. 
 
6. Composite Lines 
 
a. The minimum required number of Composite Lines to be publishe d shall be 
based on the following staffing formula: Composite Lines shall equal the 
number of scheduled Vacation weeks that begins in such Month,  divided by 
four (4), rounded up to the next whole integer (e.g., 11 w eeks of Vacation = 
11/4 = 2.75, rounded up to a minimum of 3 Composite Lines  for this Position 
and Domicile for the Month 
 
b. Composite Lines shall be blank when published in the Monthly Bid Package. 
 
c. Composite Lines shall be constructed after the completion of  SAP, as 
provided in 14.C.6. and shall be constructed with any combina tion of the 
following scheduled Assignments: Trip Pairings, Reserve Duty, Vacati on, 
Training, Scheduled Days Off and other Company-Directed Assign ments. 
 
d. A Composite Line shall be constructed with at least one (1) sched uled Day 
Off in any seven (7) consecutive Days. 
 
e. A Composite Line shall be constructed with no less than the  Minimum Days 
Off in a Month, as provided in this subsection E.2.d. 
 
f. To the extent possible, at least two (2) scheduled Days Off sh all separate 
blocks of Trip Pairings, except for the first and last Day of t he Bid Period. 
When this limitation in a Composite Line cannot be met b ecause the 
Composite Line’s PCH value is below the MPG, the sch eduled Days Off 
between Trip Pairings may be reduced to one (1) scheduled Day Off until the 
minimum MPG has been met. 
 
g. The lowest numbered Composite Line in each Position and Domicile shall be 
constructed with the highest scheduled PCH, followed by a Co mposite Line 
with the next highest PCH until all Composite Lines are co nstructed. 
 
7. Minimum Reserve Compliment 
 
a. The Company shall utilize the following criteria to determ ine the Minimum 
Reserve Compliment for the Monthly Bid Period and the daily flying schedule 
during a Bid Month; 
 
(1) When calculating the Minimum Reserve Compliment, the Company  shall 
plan on a minimum coverage of fifty percent (50%) of the avail able daily 
scheduled Trip Pairings per R1 or R2 Pilot per Position and Domi cile. 
This fifty percent (50%) Minimum Reserve Compliment shall const itute a 

--- PAGE BREAK ---

a 2:1 ratio of; (1) total number of daily Trip Pairing(s) per; (2) total number 
of Pilots on R1 or R2 per day. 
 
(2) All R1 and R2 Reserve Assignments, Reserve Assignments within Split  
Trips, and unassigned daily Open Time per Position and in each 
Domicile, shall be used to calculate the Minimum Reserve Compli ment. 
 
b. All published Reserve Assignments scheduled on  each  Day  of  the  
Month in the Initial Lines shall be  the  Minimum  Net  Reserve  
Complement for each Day in that Month. The Company may construct 
additional Reserve Assignments to cover increased flying or lack of Reserve 
Pilot coverage for any Day in the Month. 
 
c. All Reserve Assignments not constructed into Lines or are “new”  Reserve 
Assignments after the commencement of the Initial Line Bid Peri od shall be 
published in Open Time, except for those Reserve Assignments tha t are 
constructed for a Pilot that completes Long-Term Training or r eturns from a 
Leave of Absence, as provided in Section 8 (Leaves of Absence). 
 
d. Per Position and Domicile, at the beginning of the Monthly Bid Period, as well 
as the beginning of each Day of the Month, Crew Scheduling  shall 
electronically update and publish the Minimum Net Reserve re quirement and 
the number and type of Reserve Assignments that are available for each Day 
in that Month. 
 
8. Reserve Lines 
 
a. The Company shall, as provided in subsection 14.E.7., construct Reserve 
Lines utilizing the Minimum Daily Reserve Assignments and if ava ilable, any 
other additional Reserve Assignments that have been constructe d, as 
provided for in subsection 14.E.2.k.. Such Lines shall contain  only Reserve 
Assignments. As provided in Section 15 (Reserve), the types of Reserve 
Assignments that may be constructed and placed onto a Reserve Li ne are: 
In-Domicile-Short Call Reserve Assignment (R1 RAP), Out- of-Domicile-Short 
Call Reserve Assignments (R2 RAP) and In-Domicile-Long-Call Rese rve 
Assignments (R-3). 
 
b. To the maximum extent possibl e, the Company shall construct each Reserve 
Line with only R-1 RAP’s  or Lines with only R-3 Reserve Assignments, except 
they may construct a Reserve Line that contains both blocks of R- 1 RAP’s 
and R-3 Reserve Assignments, so long as each block of Reserve 
Assignments contains the same type of Reserve Assignment. 
 
c. Reserve Lines containing R-2 RAPs shall be constructed with pure ly R- 2 
RAPs, except when an R-2 RAP is part of a Split-Trip Pairing. 

--- PAGE BREAK ---

d. All Days of R-1 RAPs, along with their individual DOT and D uty Off times 
shall be published in each R-1 Reserve Line. R-1 DOTs a nd Duty Off may 
be scheduled differently, from Day to Day. 
 
e. Per Position and Domicile, all Reserve Lines shall be publishe d in the 
Monthly Bid Period and available for all Eligible Pilots to  bid. 
 
f. Reserve Assignments in a Reserve Line may be scheduled as a Single -Day 
Reserve or in blocks, up to the Maximum Schedule Workdays in a Month, as 
provided in subsection 14.E.2.c.. When constructing Reserve Lines,  Single- 
Day Reserve Assignments shall be limited to the first or last Day of the Month. 
 
g. R-2 RAP’s in Reserve Lines may be scheduled either consecutively o r in 
blocks, up to the Maximum Scheduled Workday limitation, as provid ed in 
subsection 14.E.2.c. When a Pilot’s Line contains R -2 RAP’s that are 
scheduled in blocks throughout the Month, a minimum of five (5) consecutive 
Days Off in his Domicile shall be scheduled after each block of  R-2 RAP’s, 
except when a block of R- 2 RAP’s transition out of a current Month into the 
new Month, the Integration Procedures in subsection 14.F.5 . shall be 
applicable. 
 
9. Domicile Flex Lines 
 
a. Per Position and Domicile, the Company shall create Domicile Flex Lines, as 
provided for in this subsection 14.E.2.j. and 14.E.2.k. 
 
b. All Domicile Flex Lines shall be built with a minimum, singl e block of thirteen 
(13) consecutive Days Off for a thirty (30) Day Month and fourtee n (14) 
consecutive Days Off in a thirty-one (31) Day Month. 
 
c. All Workdays constructed in a Domicile Flex Line shall be R-1 R eserve 
Assignments. The Company shall publish their respective RAP Times when 
publishing such Lines for bid. 
 
d. During the Training Bid Period, Pilots in each Position and Domicile shall 
have the opportunity to request a Domicile Flex Line. 
 
e. At the completion of each Training Bid Period during a Monthl y Bid Period, 
the Company shall publish the number of available Domicile  Flex Lines for 
each Position and Domicile. 
 
f. Prior to the commencement of each Initial Line Bid Period during the Monthly 
Bid Period, the Company shall publish all Domicile Flex Lin es. 
 
g. Pilots who have submitted a Domicile Flex Line request, shall  bid for and be 
awarded a Domicile Flex Line in order of their Seniority, during the Initial Bid 

--- PAGE BREAK ---

Line Awards. Pilots who are not awarded a Domicile Flex Lin e shall have 
their alternate Bid requests honored in order of Seniority. 
 
h. The minimum Rest Requirements for a Pilot who is awarded a Domicile Flex 
Line shall be a scheduled consecutive twenty-four (24) hour period, f ree from 
all Duty, within a seven (7) consecutive Day period. 

--- PAGE BREAK ---

M. TRIP DROPS 
 
1. Unilateral Drops 
 
a. After the Final Line Awards are published, a Pilot may req uest to Drop a Trip 
Pairing or Reserve Assignment from his Line by submitting Trip 
Trade/Drop/Pick-up Form to Crew Scheduling or, the Aloha Dispat cher who 
is on Duty. Crew Scheduling shall administer the Trip Drop Process fairly 
and equitably. 
 
b. A Pilot shall be approved or for a Unilateral Drop in “real ti me” provided; 
 
(1) The Company has constructed Reserve Assignments in excess of the 
Minimum Reserve Complement, as provided in 14.E.7.a. and, 
 
(2) The Pilot’s requested Trip Pairing DOT is within any Reserve Pi lot’s R1, 
R2 or Split- Trip Pairing’s first 8 hours of Reserve DOT  and, 
 
(3) The Pilot’s requested Trip Pairing can be accomplished within the 
Reserve Pilot’s R1, R2 or Split-Trip Parings scheduled DOT and Duty- 
Off-Time, then he shall be approved for the Unilateral Trip Drop. 
 
c. If two (2) or more Pilots in the same Position submit Drop request s for 
Assignments scheduled on the same Day(s), all requests shall be ap prove d 
in Seniority Order. 
 
d. If a Unilateral Drop is denied or cannot be immediately approved as provided 
in this subsection M.1., a Pilot may request Crew Scheduling to “advertise” 
his Trip Pairing(s) or Reserve Assignments in Open Time to allow  other Pilots 
in his Position to Pick-Up or Trip Trade with his Assignment. Such  
Assignment shall remain in Open Time until; 
 
(1) the Pilot requests Crew Scheduling to remove his Assignment from being 
“advertised” in Open Time; or,  
 
(2) such Assignment is Picked-up by or Trip-Traded with another Pilot;  or, 
 
(3) if either (1) or (2) has not occurred twenty-four (24) hours prior t o the 
Assignment’s  DOT, in which case Crew Scheduling shall remove the Trip 
Pairing from Open Time, inform the Pilot that his Trip Drop h as been 
denied, and the Pilot shall remain responsible for the Assig nment. 
 
e. Trip drop requests that are put into Open Time, as provided in this subsection 
M.1.d., shall be offered at 100% PCH of the Trip Pairing  dropped and 
published into Open Time. Pilot’s  requesting to pick up the same dropped 

--- PAGE BREAK ---

Trip Pairing shall be notified by Crew Scheduling that it is only being offered 
at 100% of the PCH value. 
 
f. At the discretion of the Company, approved Trip Drop’s shall be  posted in 
Open Time as provided in this subsection, M.1.e., or withhe ld from Open 
Time and assigned to a Reserve Pilot provided in this subsecti on M.1.b. 
Nothing in this subsection shall prohibit the Company from po sting the Trip 
Drop in Open Time or assigning the Trip from the VPA List or the JA process. 
 
2. Partial Trip Drops 
 
a. A Pilot may request to drop a portion of his Trip Pairing (Part ial Trip Drop). 
Crew Scheduling shall approve or deny all Partial Trip Drop requests. Except 
as provided in subsection 14.M.3. (Deadhead Drops), all Partia l Trip Drops 
shall be subject to the provisions of subsection 14.L.1. 
 
b. The Company shall not be responsible to provide Per Diem  or Deadhead Pay 
for any unscheduled Deadhead that results from a Pilot’s Partial  Trip Drop. 
 
3. Deadhead Drops 
 
a. A Pilot may request to Drop a scheduled Deadhead when  it is the first and/or 
last segment(s) of his Duty Assignment. If Crew Scheduling has no f urther 
potential Duty for that Pilot in that Duty Period, Deadhe ad Drops shall be 
approved as follows: 
 
b. When the Deadhead Segment(s) is on a Company Aircraft, the Drop request 
must be made no later than six (6) hours before the DOT of the  Deadhead. 
 
c. If the scheduled Deadhead is on another Commercial Air Carrier,  the Pilot 
shall make his Drop request, as provided in Section 7 (Deadhea ding). 
 
d.  A Pilot who was originally scheduled to Deadhead to and/or from his Domicile 
or TDY Location shall be compensated, as provided in Section 3  
(Compensation) for all approved Dropped Deadhead Segments. 
 
IN WITNESS WHEREOF, the parties hereto have signed this LOA eff ective September 1, 2020: 
 
For the Union: For the Company:
