LETTER OF AGREEMENT  #15 
By and Between 
NORTHERN AIR CARGO,  INC. 
and the 
AIRLINE PILOTS  
in the service of 
NORTHERN AIR CARGO, INC.  
as represented by  
THE INTERNATIONAL BROTHERHOOD OF TEAMSTERS  
RE: SECTION 2, DEFINITIONS, SECTION 3.S., INSTRUCTOR PILOT, CHECK AIRMAN AND 
AIRCREW PROGRAM DESIGNEE PREMIUMS, SECTIONS 14.D., 14.E. AND 14.M. TO 
INCLUDE DOMICILE FLEX LINES AND TRIP DROP PROVISIONS  
THIS LETTER OF AGREEMENT is made and entere d into in accordance with the provisions of 
the Railway Labor Act, as amended, by and between NORTHERN AIR CARGO, INC (the 
“Company”) and the INTERNATIONAL BROTHERHOOD OF TEAMSTERS (the “Union”).  
WHEREAS additions to Section 2, Definitions are required for newly created terminology; and  
WHEREAS the parties, recognize the need to fairly compensate Instructors, Check Airmen and 
Aircrew Program Designees (APD’s) commensurate with their additional obligations and 
responsibilities, as provided in su bsection 3.S.; and  
WHEREAS the parties wish to improve Line Construction options for the Pilots with the creation 
of Domicile Flex Lines; and  
WHEREAS  the parties  wish to create  a more  defined  structure  that provides  better  guidance  when 
the Company is determining whether to “approve” or “deny” a Trip Drop request from a Pilot, as 
provided in subsection 14.M;  and 
WHERAS the parties agree that the provisions contained in this Letter of Agreement (LOA) shall 
supersede the previous exis ting provisions in subsections 3.S.,14.D., 14.E. and 14.M. of this 
Agreement.  
NOW, THEREFORE, it is mutually agreed that:  

--- PAGE BREAK ---

SECTION 2 
DEFINITIONS  
 
A Ghost Bid  A Line that a Full -Time Check Airman or Instructor Pilot has bid for, 
and as a result of his ineligibility to bid for that Month, as provided in 
subsection 14.C., he shall not be awarded a Line that would have 
been awarded had it not been for his Full -Time Check Airman or 
Instructor  status  for that Month,  but through  such  Ghost  Bid, he shall 
retain  such  Initial  Line’s  PCH  for the purpose  of establishing  his new 
MPG for that Month. All Ghost Bids shall be awarded in Seniority 
Order, in relation to his Position in his  Domicile.  

--- PAGE BREAK ---

SECTION 3 
COMPENSATION  
 
S. AIRCREW PROGRAM DESIGNEE, CHECK AIRMAN AND INSTRUCTOR PILOT 
PREMIUMS  
 
1. All Line Check Airman (LCA) and/or Simulator Check Airman (SCA), to include 
Aircrew Program Designee(s) (APD’s) and Check Airman performing ground 
school instruction, in addition to Section 3, Compensat ion, shall receive the 
following  premiums;  
 
a. All Check Airman shall receive a monthly override of 10% for all cumulative 
PCH in a Monthly Bid  Period.  
 
b. An APD shall receive an override of $75.00 per hour above his adjusted 
Check Airman hourly pay rate as pro vided in Section 3.S.1.a., for all training 
and checking events while serving in the capacity of an  APD.  
 
c. All Check Airman shall receive an override of $50.00 per hour above his 
adjusted Check Airman hourly pay rate as provided in Section 3.S.1.a., for 
all training, checking, simulator, ground school and briefing events when 
acting in the capacity of a Check  Airman.  
 
d. Check  Airman  performing  administrative  duties  at the direction  of the Training 
Department  shall be credited  for such  duty as provided  for in Section  3.S.1.a.  
 
e. The minimum PCH for a Check Airman performing an Assignment shall not 
be less than the  DPG.  
 
2. Simulator and/or Ground School instructors, in addition to Section 3, 
Compensation, shall receive the following  premiums;  
 
a. A simulator and/or ground school instructor performing simulator or ground 
school training event(s), shall receive an override of $35.00 per hour above 
his hourly pay rate as provided in Section 3, Appendix A,  Compensation.  
 
b. A Simulator and/or Ground School I nstructor shall receive a 10% hourly 
override  on a Day-by-Day basis,  for any administrative  duty performed  at the 
direction of the Training  Department.  
 
c. The minimum PCH for a Simulator or Ground School Instructor shall not be 
less than the  DPG.  
 
3. Ghost Bids 

--- PAGE BREAK ---

a. When a Check Airman is unable to bid for a Line, as provided in Section 
14.C.4.b.(4).,  he shall be afforded  the opportunity  to “Ghost  Bid” for a Line of 
Flying  during  the Initial  Line Bid Period,  as provided  in subsections  14.C.6  or 
14.C.7. A Pilot who Ghost Bids shall not be awarded a Line during the Initial 
Line Bid Period.  
 
b. The Ghost Bid Award shall become a Pilot’s new MPG for the  Month.  
 
c. As provided in subsection 3.S.3.b., his new MPG, as the result of his Ghost 
Bid, shall be use d when calculating a Check Airman’s Monthly Cumulative 
PCH, as provided in subsection  3.N. 
 
d. A Check Airman shall be paid for all Premiums and additional PCH earned 
during the Month above his new MPG, resulting from his Ghost Bid, as 
provided for in Section  3 (Compensation).  
 
e. A Check Airman or Instructor Pilot who Ghost Bids shall be available to be 
scheduled by the Training Department to perform Training Duties, as 
provided in Section  22.D.  
 
4. General  
 
a. When an Instructor, Check Airman or APD is Assigned to perform Training 
on a lesser -paid Aircraft Type, he shall receive the applicable Hourly Pay 
Rate for the Position his system -wide Seniority allows him to hold for all 
earned PCH in the Month, provided he bids for and is awarded a Vacancy 
(“Phantom Award”) in the higher paying  Position.  
 
b. A Check  Airman  performing  an Assignment  on a scheduled  Day Off, he shall 
be paid one hundred and fifty percent (150%) of his applicable Hourly Pay 
Rate in addition to the provisions  provided in Section 3.S.1 and 3.S.2.  
Such compensation shall be paid in addition to all PCH accumulated during 
a Month, as provided in subsection  3.N. 
 
5. Flight Operations shall consider current Check Airman recommendations when 
selecting new Check Airman or Instructors during the respective Vacancy 
Process.  

--- PAGE BREAK ---

SECTION 14 
SCHEDULING  
 
D. TRIP PAIRING  CONSTRUCTION  
 
1. A Trip Pairing shall consist of one (1) or more Duty Periods and contain any 
mixture of Flight and/or Deadhead Segm ents, and under limited circumstances 
R-1 or R -2 RAPs, as provided for in this subsection  14.D.  
 
2. The Company  shall construct,  to the greatest  extent  possible,  Trip Pairings  in the 
following order of  prioritization:  
 
a. The maximum number of Trip Pairings with Flight Segments and/or 
Deadhead Segments,  then,  
 
b. Trip Pairings with Reserve Assignments and/or Split -Trip Pairings, as 
provided in  14.D.3.  
 
3. Trip Pairings shall be constructed utilizing all “Known Flying” at the 
commencement of each Month’s In itial Line Bid Period as provided in  Section  
14.C.6. Known Flying shall be defined as all Flight Segments known to be 
performed by the Company prior to the commencement of each Monthly Initial 
Line Bid Period. When the Company has been contracted to perfor m Charters, 
Ad-Hoc or ACMI contracts, all such Flying shall also be included in that Month’s 
Known Flying. No less than five (5) Days prior to the commencement of each 
Initial  Line Bid Period,  the Company  shall provide  the JSC with a list of all Known 
Flying, their initial draft of Trip Pairings and Lines for each Position, in all 
Domiciles.  
 
4. For Flight  Segments  or RAP’s  that originate  and/or  end at a location  other  than a 
Pilot’s Domicile, the Company shall schedule Deadhead segments on the front  
and back end of such Trip Pairings in order to reposition the Pilot from his 
Domicile  or his Primary  Residence  if on an R3, to and from such  Out-of-Domicile 
location. The Company shall schedule all such Deadhead segments in a Trip 
Pairing as far in advanc e as possible.  
 
5. If during Trip Pairing construction, as provided in subsection 14.D.2., the 
Company has an additional need for Reserve staffing in a specific Position in a 
Domicile; or the PCH of a Trip Pairing is less than the DPG, they may construct 
a Split-Trip Pairing utilizing Known Flying Flight Segments, or a modified R -1 or 
R-2 Reserve Assignment. Such Split -Trip Pairings may be constructed and may 
be used to assist in meeting the Regular Line construction requirements, as 
provided in subsection 14. E.5. Split Trips shall be constructed as  follows:  
 
a. Trip Pairings with R -1 RAPs, Trip Pairings and Deadhead Segments when 
the RAP is scheduled to be performed in a Company designated  Domicile.  

--- PAGE BREAK ---

 
b. Trip Pairings with R -2 RAPs, Trip Pairings and Deadhead Segments when 
the R-2 RAP is scheduled  to be performed  at a location  other  than a Domicile.  
 
6. If an R1 or R2 RAP follows the last Flight and/or Deadhead Segment in a single 
Duty Period  and a Pilot has not received  another  Duty Assignment  within  one (1) 
hour after Block -In of his previous  Assignment  in that same  Duty Period,  he shall 
be released  from the remaining  portion  of his scheduled  Duty and paid for all Duty 
he performed and for the scheduled Duty that was dropped due to such  release, 
as provided in Section 3  (Compensation).  
 
7. Trip Pairing construction may also contain Deadhead Segments and Reserve 
Availability  Periods  (RAP’s).  After  the start of each  Month’s  Initial  Line Bid Period 
any new Flight  Segments  that becomes  Known  Flying shall be constructed  into a 
Trip Pairing(s) and the subsequently put into Open Time or Assigned to a 
Reserve Pilot as provided for in this Agreement.  
 
8. The maximum duration of a single Trip Pairing that originates and ends in the 
same Month shall not ex ceed seventeen (17) consecutive Days (inclusive of all 
scheduled  Rest Periods  within  such  Trip Pairing)  when  constructed  into an Initial 
Line.  
 
9. The maximum duration of a single Trip Pairing that originates in one Month and 
ends in the following Month (inclusive of all scheduled Rest Periods), , shall not 
exceed more than twenty (20) consecutive Days and shall abide by the 
provisions, as provided for in this Section 14.E.2.c., and 14.E.2.d. when 
constructed into an Initial  Line.  
 
1 0. The maximum duration of  a single Trip Pairing in a TDY Line that originates and 
ends in the same Month shall not exceed eighteen (18) Days (inclusive of all 
scheduled Rest Periods), when constructed into an Initial  Line.  
 
1 1.  The maximum duration of a single Trip Pairing in a TDY L ine that originates in 
one Month and ends in the following Month (inclusive of all scheduled Rest 
Periods), , shall not exceed more than twenty (20) consecutive Days and shall 
abide by the provisions as provided for in this Section 14.E.2.c., and 14.E.2.d.  
when constructed into an Initial  Line.  
 
1 2.  All other  Trip Pairings  that are constructed  after the publishing  of the Initial  Lines 
shall follow the same maximum duration limitations, as provided for in 
subsections 14.D.8., 14.D.9, 14.D.10. and  14.D.11.  
 
1 3. The portion  of a Trip Pairing,  as provided  for in subsections  14.D.9  and 14.D.11., 
that “transitions” into the following Month, shall be integrated, as provided in 
subsection 14.F.5 (Month -End Integration.  

--- PAGE BREAK ---

E. MONTHLY LINE OF FLYING CONSTRU CTION  PARAMETERS  
 
1. The published  Initial  Lines  shall be constructed  as Regular,  Reserve,  Composite 
and Domicile Flex Lines, as provided for in this subsection 14.E. Except as 
otherwise provided in this Section 14, all Lines shall be bid for and awarded in 
Seniority  Order,  in each  Position,  per Domicile.  Each  Position  and Domicile  shall 
utilize either the Primary or Secondary Bid Process, as authorized by the  JSC.  
 
2. The prioritization for constructing Initial Lines, in the following sequential orde r, 
shall be administered each Month when constructing all Lines for each Position 
in a Domicile:  
 
a. The total number of constructed Initial Lines, Including Domicile Flex Lines, 
shall equal and not exceed the number of its bidding Pilots in each Position 
at a Domicile for that  Month.  
 
b. All Regular,  Composite,  Reserve  and Domicile  Flex Lines  shall have  at least 
two (2) separate  periods  of at least  three  (3) consecutive  Days  Off or a single 
block of at least five (5) consecutive Days Off.  
 
c. All published  Initial  Lines  (i.e. Regular,  Composite,  Reserve,  or Domicile  Flex 
Lines) during the Monthly Bid Period shall be constructed with no more than 
seventeen (17) scheduled Workdays in any given Month (including all 
scheduled Duty and/or other Company -Directed  Assignments).  
 
d. The Minimum scheduled Days Off in all constructed Initial Lines shall be 
thirteen (13) Days Off for a thirty (30) Day Month and fourteen (14) Days Off 
in thirty -one (31) Day  Month.  
 
e. All scheduled  Days  Off in the published  Initial  and Final  Line awards  shall be 
scheduled in the Pilot’s  Domicile.  
 
f. All Initial Lines shall be constructed to be no greater than ninety -five (95) 
PCH.  Any Trip Pairings  not constructed  in a Line shall be placed  into in Open 
Time.  
 
g. Regular Lines shall be constructed first with Trips from all of the Month’s 
Known  Flying.  
 
(1) The Company shall, to the maximum extent possible construct Trip 
Pairings with the highest PCH into Regular Lines and holdback Trip 
Pairings with a lesser PCH value in Open Time, however, the Company 
shall not be restricted from optimizing Regular Line Construction by 
substituting or adding the minimum number of lower PCH Trip Pairings 
for higher PCH Trip Pairings to maximize the number of Regular Lines 
constructed.  

--- PAGE BREAK ---

 
(2) The Company  shall build  the maximum  number  of Regular  Lines,  without 
any Reserve Assignments, for each Initial Line Bid  Period.  
 
(3) Once such “pure” Regular Lines cannot be constructed, the Company 
may then continue to build Regular Lines with Trip Pairings to in clude 
Reserve Assignments as provided in subsection  14.E.5.a.  
 
h. When constructing Regular Lines, the lowest numbered published Line  shall 
be constructed with the maximum PCH. The following lowest numbered 
Regular  Line shall be constructed  with the same  or less PCH  as the previous 
Line. This shall continue in this sequence until the last Regular Line 
constructed that results in reducing the Trip Pairing PCH for that specific 
Position  and Domicile  to a level at least  below  fifteen  percent  (15%)  PCH,  but 
great er than three percent (3%) of such total  PCH.  
 
i. Once the Initial phase of the Regular Lines has concluded, the required 
Composite and Reserve Lines, as provided in this Section 14, shall be 
constructed.  In the event  there  is an inadequate  number  of Pilots  to build  the 
required number of Reserve and/or Composite Lines in a Position at a 
Domicile,  the Company  may construct  R2 Reserve  Lines  in another  Domicile 
to supplement temporary staffing deficits in such Domicile. In all cases, 
Composite  Line const ruction  shall supersede  Reserve  Line construction  and 
Regular  Line construction  shall supersede  both Composite  and Reserve  Line 
construction.  
 
j. If three (3) or more Reserve Lines are constructed and there are Pilots 
requesting to bid for Domicile Flex Lines, fifty percent (50%) of the Reserve 
Lines, rounded up to the nearest whole integer, shall be constructed as 
Domicile Flex Lines for those pilo ts requesting a Domicile Flex  Line.  
 
k. Once it is determined how many Domicile Flex Lines shall be published and 
if additional Lines that can be built utilizing the construction parameters in 
subsection 14.E.6., the Company, in consultation with the JSC, sha ll 
construct additional Regular and/or Reserve Lines until no other Lines can 
be constructed. When additional Reserve Lines are created and if there are 
additional  Pilots  who are requesting  to bid for Domicile  Flex Lines,  such  Lines 
shall be constructed  using the ratio as provided  for in this subsection  14.E.2.j.  
 
3. All TDY Lines shall be constructed as other Lines, with the following  exceptions:  
 
a. All Trip Pairings  in a TDY Line,  shall be scheduled  to originate  and end at the 
TDY Location, except for Trip Pairings to and from his Domicile and a TDY 
Location.  

--- PAGE BREAK ---

b. When Reserve Duty Periods are constructed in a TDY Line, they shall Duty 
On and Duty Off at the TDY Location, except as provided elsewhere in this 
Section  14. 
 
c. All published TDY Lines during t he Monthly Bid Period shall be constructed 
with no more  than eighteen  (18) scheduled  Workdays  in a Month  inclusive  of 
any Deadhead between a Pilot’s Primary Residence and the location(s) 
where his TDY Assignment is scheduled to originate and/or  end. 
 
d. For all TDY Lines, the minimum Days Off requirement shall be twelve (12) 
Days Off in a thirty (30) Day Month and thirteen (13) Days Off in a thirty -one 
Day Month.  
 
e. At least  fifty percent  (50%)  of TDY Lines  shall be scheduled  to begin  and end 
in the same Mo nth. The remaining TDY Lines may be scheduled to “carry 
over” into the subsequent Month.  
 
f. Scheduled Days Off within a block of Workdays at a TDY Location shall not 
be considered a Day Off for the purposes of meeting the Pilot’s Minimum 
Days Off in Domicile  requirement.  
 
4. All published Initial Lines that are constructed and awarded during the Initial Bid 
Period, and except as provided for in Section 8 (Leaves of Absence), all Final 
Awarded and Assigned Lines at the conclusion of the Monthly Bid Period, shall 
be valued at no less than MPG, as provided in Section 3  (Compensation).  
 
5. Regular Lines  
 
a. A Regular Line is a planned sequence created solely of Trip Pairings in a 
Month, except when maximizing the number of Regular Lines in a Position 
and Domicile, as provided for in subsections 14.E.2.g. The maximum 
number of R -1 RAP’s in any given Regular Line shall not exceed six  (6). 
 
b. Regular Lines shall be constructed and published during the Initial Line Bid 
Period, as provided in subsections 14.C.6. and/or 14.C.7 . and this  14.E.  
 
c. A Regular Line shall be constructed with at least one (1) scheduled Day Off 
in any seven (7) consecutive  Days.  
 
d. To the maximum extent possible, per Position and Domicile, the Company 
shall construct Regular Lines with blocks of Workdays that are scheduled 
with consistent Weekly work patterns and Report Times (e.g., Workdays 
scheduled on Sunday through Thursday each Week, or as close to a  weekly 
Workday pattern, all AM or PM DOT’s for scheduled Assignments) 
throughout  the Month.  This provision  shall not be utilized  if doing  so would  

--- PAGE BREAK ---

prohibit  the Company  from adhering  to the other  provisions  in this subsectio n 
14.E.  
 
e. To the maximum extent possible, a Regular Line shall not be constructed 
with single Days Off during the Month, except for the first or the last Day of 
the Month. When this limitation cannot be avoided, due to the inability to 
construct  a Regular  Line to the MPG,  a Regular  Line may be constructed  with 
the minimum number of scheduled single Days Off in a Month in order to 
achieve such  requirement.  
 
f. All Trip Pairings  in a Regular  Line shall be scheduled  to begin  and end at the 
Pilot’s Domicile. In the event of a TDY Vacancy Award, it may be either his 
Domicile or Residence Airport, as defined in Section 15.B.4.c., Reserves. 
Once he is in his TDY Location, all subsequent Trip Pairings shall begin  and 
end in that  location.  
 
g. R-3 Reserve Assignments shall not be scheduled onto Regular  Lines.  
 
h. To the maximum Extent Possible, the Company shall schedule all Night  Trip 
Pairings consecutively when they are constructed into a Regular  Line.  
 
i. In-Domicile:  
 
(1) No more than four (4) consecutive  Night Trip Pairings in - Domicile shall 
be scheduled in a row without at least two (2) consecutive Scheduled 
Days Off.  
 
(2) A Night Trip Pairing that originates and ends in -Domicile shall not be 
scheduled to Duty Off the Day before the following scheduled Nigh t Trip 
Pairing’s DOT in his Line, nor shall a Night Trip Pairing’s DOT be 
scheduled  the Day after the previous  Night  Trip Pairing’s  scheduled  Duty 
Off Time (“no  staggering”).  
 
j. Out-of-Domicile:  
 
(1) When constructing Multi -day Trip Pairings out-of-Domicile, to include 
Ferry Flight or Deadhead Segments, the Company shall, to the best of 
their ability, not stagger Night Flight Assignments within a Trip Pairing 
(“no staggering”).  
 
(2) Multi -day Trip Pairings Out -of-Domicile, to include Ferry Flight or 
Deadhead Segments, shall not be scheduled for more than 4 
consecutive Night Trip Pairing Assignments. A minimum of two (2) 
consecutive  Days  of Reserve  Assignments  shall follow  any 4 consecutive 
Night  Trip Assignments.  During  such  two Days  of Reserve  Assignments, 
the Company  shall be responsible  for scheduling  a continuous  twenty - 

--- PAGE BREAK ---

four (24) hour Rest Period for such Pilot, free from all Duty, before he is 
required to perform his next Duty Assignment.  
 
6. Composite  Lines  
 
a. The minimum required number of Composite Lines to be published shall be 
based on the following staffing formula: Composite Lines shall equal the 
number of scheduled Vacation weeks that begins in such Month, divided by 
four (4), rounded up to the next whole int eger (e.g., 11 weeks of Vacation = 
11/4 = 2.75,  rounded  up to a minimum  of 3 Composite  Lines  for this Position 
and Domicile for the  Month  
 
b. Composite  Lines  shall be blank when  published  in the Monthly  Bid Package.  
 
c. Composite Lines shall be constructed after  the completion of SAP, as 
provided in 14.C.6. and shall be constructed with any combination of the 
following scheduled Assignments: Trip Pairings, Reserve Duty, Vacation, 
Training, Scheduled Days Off and other Company -Directed  Assignments.  
 
d. A Composite Line shall be constructed with at least one (1) scheduled Day 
Off in any seven (7) consecutive  Days.  
 
e. A Composite Line shall be constructed with no less than the Minimum Days 
Off in a Month, as provided in this subsection  E.2.d.  
 
f. To the extent po ssible, at least two (2) scheduled Days Off shall separate 
blocks of Trip Pairings, except for the first and last Day of the Bid Period. 
When this limitation in a Composite Line cannot be met because the 
Composite Line’s PCH value is below the MPG, the sch eduled Days Off 
between  Trip Pairings  may be reduced  to one (1) scheduled  Day Off until the 
minimum MPG has been  met. 
 
g. The lowest  numbered  Composite  Line in each  Position  and Domicile  shall be 
constructed with the highest scheduled PCH, followed by a Composite Line 
with the next highest PCH until all Composite Lines are  constructed.  
 
7. Minimum Reserve  Compliment  
 
a. The Company shall utilize the following criteria to determine the Minimum 
Reserve  Compliment  for the Monthly  Bid Period  and the daily flying  schedule 
during a Bid  Month;  
 
(1) When  calculating  the Minimum  Reserve  Compliment,  the Company  shall 
plan on a minimum coverage of fifty percent (50%) of the available daily 
scheduled Trip Pairings per R1 or R2 Pilot per Position and Domicile. 
This fifty percent  (50%)  Minimum  Reserve  Compliment  shall constitute  a 

--- PAGE BREAK ---

a 2:1 ratio of; (1) total number  of daily Trip Pairing(s)  per; (2) total number 
of Pilots on R1 or R2 per  day. 
 
(2) All R1 and R2 Reserve Assignments, Reserve Assignments within Split 
Trips, and unassigned daily Open Time per Position and in each 
Domicile, shall be used to calculate the Minimum Reserve  Compliment.  
 
b. All published Reserve Assignments scheduled on  each  Day  of  the  
Month in the Initial Lines shall be  the  Minimum  Net  Reserve  
Complement for each Day in that Month. The Company may construct 
additional  Reserve  Assignments  to cover  increased  flying  or lack of Reserve 
Pilot coverage for any Day in the  Month.  
 
c. All Reserve Assignments not constructed into Lines or are “new”  Reserve 
Assignments after the commencement of the Initial Line Bid Period shall be 
published in Open Time, except for those Reserve Assignments that are 
constructed for a Pilot that completes Long -Term Training or returns from a 
Leave of Absence, as provi ded in Section 8 (Leaves of  Absence).  
 
d. Per Position  and Domicile,  at the beginning  of the Monthly  Bid Period,  as well 
as the beginning of each Day of the Month, Crew Scheduling shall 
electronically  update  and publish  the Minimum  Net Reserve  requirement  and 
the number  and type of Reserve  Assignments  that are available  for each  Day 
in that  Month.  
 
8. Reserve  Lines  
 
a. The Company shall, as provided in subsection 14.E.7., construct Reserve 
Lines utilizing the Minimum Daily Reserve Assignments and if available,  any 
other additional Reserve Assignments that have been constructed, as 
provided for in subsection 14.E.2.k.. Such Lines shall contain only Reserve 
Assignments. As provided in Section 15 (Reserve), the types of Reserve 
Assignm ents that may be constructed and placed onto a Reserve Line are: 
In-Domicile -Short  Call Reserve  Assignment  (R1 RAP),  Out-of-Domicile -Short 
Call Reserve Assignments (R2 RAP) and In -Domicile -Long -Call Reserve 
Assignments (R -3). 
 
b. To the maximum  extent  possibl e, the Company  shall construct  each  Reserve 
Line with only R-1 RAP’s  or Lines  with only R-3 Reserve  Assignments,  except 
they may construct a Reserve Line that contains both blocks of R -1 RAP’s 
and R -3 Reserve Assignments, so long as each block of Reserve 
Assignments contains the same type of Reserve  Assignment.  
 
c. Reserve Lines containing R -2 RAPs shall be constructed with purely R -2 
RAPs, except when an R -2 RAP is part of a Split -Trip Pairing.  

--- PAGE BREAK ---

d. All Days of R -1 RAPs, along with their individual DOT and Duty Off times 
shall be published in each R -1 Reserve Line. R -1 DOTs and Duty Off may 
be scheduled  differently, from Day to  Day. 
 
e. Per Position and Domicile, all Reserve Lines shall be published in the 
Monthly Bid Period and available for all Eligible Pilots to  bid. 
 
f. Reserve Assignments in a Reserve Line may be scheduled as a Single -Day 
Reserve  or in blocks,  up to the Maximum  Schedule  Workdays  in a Month,  as 
provided in subsection 14.E.2.c.. When constructing Reserve Lines, Single - 
Day Reserve  Assignments  shall be limited  to the first or last Day of the Month.  
 
g. R-2 RAP’s in Reserve Lines may be scheduled either consecutively or in 
blocks, up to the Maximum Scheduled Workday limitation, as provided in 
subsection 14.E.2.c. When a Pilot’s Line contains R -2 RAP’s that are 
scheduled  in blocks  throughout  the Month,  a minimum  of five (5) consecutive 
Days Off in his Domicile shall be scheduled after each block of R-2 RAP’s, 
except when a block of R -2 RAP’s transition out of a current Month into the 
new Month, the Integration Procedures in subsection 14.F.5. shall be 
appli cable.  
 
9. Domicile Flex  Lines  
 
a. Per Position  and Domicile,  the Company  shall create  Domicile  Flex Lines,  as 
provided for in this subsection 14.E.2.j. and  14.E.2.k.  
 
b. All Domicile Flex Lines shall be built with a minimum, single block of  thirteen  
(13) consecutive Days Off for a thirty (30) Day Month and fourteen (14) 
consecutive Days Off in a thirty -one (31) Day Month.  
 
c. All Workdays constructed in a Domicile Flex Line shall be R -1 Reserve 
Assignments. The Company shall publish their respective RAP Times  when 
publishing such Lines for  bid. 
 
d. During the Training Bid Period, Pilots in each Position and Domicile shall 
have the opportunity to request a Domicile Flex  Line.  
 
e. At the completion of each Training Bid Period during a Monthly Bid Period, 
the Company s hall publish the number of available Domicile Flex Lines for 
each Position and  Domicile.  
 
f. Prior  to the commencement  of each  Initial  Line Bid Period  during  the Monthly 
Bid Period, the Company shall publish all Domicile Flex  Lines.  
 
g. Pilots who have submitted a Domicile Flex Line request, shall bid for and be 
awarded a Domicile Flex Line in order of their Seniority, during the Initial  Bid 

--- PAGE BREAK ---

Line Awards. Pilots who are not awarded a Domicile Flex Line shall have 
their alternate Bid requests honored in order of Seniority.  
 
h. The minimum  Rest Requirements  for a Pilot who is awarded  a Domicile  Flex 
Line shall be a scheduled  consecutive  twenty -four (24) hour period,  free from 
all Duty, within a seven (7) consecutive Day  period.  

--- PAGE BREAK ---

M. TRIP DROPS  
 
1. Unilateral  Drops  
 
a. After  the Final  Line Awards  are published,  a Pilot may request  to Drop  a Trip 
Pairing or Reserve Assignment from his Line by submitting Trip 
Trade/Drop/Pick -up Form to Crew Scheduling or, the Aloha Dispatcher who 
is on Duty. Crew Scheduling shall administer the Trip Drop Process fairly 
and equitably.  
 
b. A Pilot shall be approved or for a Unilateral Drop in “real time”  provided;  
 
(1) The Company has constructed Reserve Assignments in excess of the 
Minimum Reserve Complement, as  provided in 14.E.7.a.  and, 
 
(2) The Pilot’s requested Trip Pairing DOT is within any Reserve Pilot’s R1, 
R2 or Split -Trip Pairing’s first 8 hours of Reserve DOT  and, 
 
(3) The Pilot’s requested Trip Pairing can be accomplished within the 
Reserve Pilot’s R1, R2 or Split -Trip Parings scheduled DOT and Duty - 
Off-Time, then he shall be approved for the Unilateral Trip  Drop.  
 
c. If two (2) or more Pilots in the same Position submit Drop requests for 
Assignments scheduled on the same Day(s), all requests shall be approve d 
in Seniority  Order.  
 
d. If a Unilateral  Drop  is denied  or cannot  be immediately  approved  as provided 
in this subsection M.1., a Pilot may request Crew Scheduling to “advertise” 
his Trip Pairing(s)  or Reserve  Assignments  in Open  Time  to allow  other  Pilots 
in his Position to Pick -Up or Trip Trade with his Assignment. Such 
Assignment shall remain in Open Time  until;  
 
(1) the Pilot requests  Crew  Scheduling  to remove  his Assignment  from being 
“advertised” in Open Time; or,  
 
(2) such Assignment is Picked -up by or Trip -Traded with another Pilot;  or, 
 
(3) if either (1) or (2) has not occurred twenty -four (24) hours prior to the 
Assignment’s  DOT,  in which  case  Crew  Scheduling  shall remove  the Trip 
Pairing from Open Time, inform the Pilot that his Trip Drop  has been 
denied, and the Pilot shall remain responsible for the  Assignment.  
 
e. Trip drop requests  that are put into Open  Time,  as provided  in this subsection 
M.1.d., shall be offered at 100% PCH of the Trip Pairing dropped and 
published  into Open  Time.  Pilot’s  requesting  to pick up the same  dropped  

--- PAGE BREAK ---

Trip Pairing shall be notified by Crew Scheduling that it is only being offered 
at 100% of the PCH value.  
 
f. At the discretion of the Company, approved Trip Drop’s shall be posted in 
Open Time as provided in this subsection, M.1.e., or withheld from Open 
Time and assigned to a Reserve Pilot provided in this subsection M.1.b. 
Nothing in this subsection shall prohibit the Company from posting the Trip 
Drop  in Open  Time  or assigning  the Trip from the VPA List or the JA process.  
 
2. Partial Trip  Drops  
 
a. A Pilot may request to drop a portion of his Trip Pairing (Partial Trip Drop). 
Crew  Scheduling  shall approve  or deny  all Partial  Trip Drop  requests.  Except 
as provided in subsection 14.M.3. (Deadhead Drops), all Partial Trip Drops 
shall be subject to the provisions of subsection  14.L.1.  
 
b. The Company  shall not be responsible  to provide  Per Diem  or Deadhead  Pay 
for any unscheduled Deadhead that results from a Pilot’s Partial Trip  Drop.  
 
3. Deadhead  Drops  
 
a. A Pilot may request  to Drop  a scheduled  Deadhead  when  it is the first and/or 
last segment(s) of his Duty Assignment. If Crew Scheduling has no further 
potential Duty for that Pilot in that Duty Period, Deadhead Drops shall be 
approved as  follows:  
 
b. When  the Deadhead  Segment(s)  is on a Company  Aircraft,  the Drop  request 
must be made no later than six (6) hours before the DOT of the  Deadhead.  
 
c. If the scheduled Deadhead is on another Commercial Air Carrier, the Pilot 
shall make his Drop request, as provided in Section 7  (Deadheading).  
 
d.  A Pilot who was originally  scheduled  to Deadhead  to and/or  from his Domicile 
or TDY Location shall be compensated, as provided in Section 3 
(Compensation) for all approved Dropped Deadhead  Segments.  
 
IN W ITNESS WHEREOF, the parties hereto have signed this LOA effective September 1, 2020:

LETTER OF AGREEMENT  # 16 
By and Between  
NORTHERN AIR CARGO, LLC  
and the  
AIRLINE PILOTS  
in the service of  
NORTHERN AIR CARGO, LLC.  
as Represented by  
THE INTERNATIONAL BROTHERHOOD OF TEAMSTERS  
This Letter of Agreement (“LOA”) is made and entered into by and between Northern 
Aviation Services, LLC (“NAS” or the “Parent”), its successors and assigns, Northern Air 
Cargo (“NAC” or the “Company”), its successors and assigns, and the Pilots in the 
services of NAC as represented by the International Brotherhood of Teamsters, Airline 
Division (collectively, the “Parties”).  As used herein, “NAC” or the “Company” shall 
include Aloha Air Cargo (“Aloha”) unless context indicates differently.  
WHEREAS Carri er A is an acquisition target of NAS; and  
WHEREAS the Parties and NAC’s pilots recognize that adding Carrier A to the NAS family 
of companies will inure to their mutual benefit;  
1. If NAS or an Affiliate is successful in acquiring Carrier A, when the acquisition
transaction is complete Northern Aviation Services will be the Parent of Carrier
A and Carrier A will be an Affiliate for all purposes under the Collective
Bargaining Agreeme nt (“CBA”) and all related letters of agreement, subject to
the terms of this LOA.  This LOA shall continue in full force and effect
irrespective of any Successor Transaction, as defined in subsection 1.F of the
CBA, undertaken in respect of NAS or NAC, or  any successor thereto, and shall
be an irrevocable and material condition of any such Successor Transaction,
and shall be binding on any Successor (as defined in subsection 1.F) to NAS
or NAC, or any Successor thereto).

--- PAGE BREAK ---

2. When the acquisition transaction is complete, Carrier A’s operations and its 
pilots will be exempted from  the terms of the CBA and any related Letters of 
Agreement or Memoranda of Understanding.   This exemption will be lost or 
otherwise cease to be effective only pursuant to paragraph 9 o r 12, below.   The 
pilots employed by Carrier A will be represented by IBT only pursuant to 
certification by the National Mediation Board or if they become employed by 
NAC.  
 
3. Following acquisition of Carrier A, Carrier A may be operated indefinitely as a 
separate subsidiary of NAS, unless and until management provides written 
notice to IBT of its intent to fully merge the operations of Carrier A with those 
of NAC. In such event, this LOA will remain in force, and the operations of 
Carrier A and NAC will be fe nced, pending completion of the procedures of 
Section 1.G. of the CBA.   Upon completion of Section 1.G procedures, this LOA 
shall become null and void unless otherwise agreed to by the parties.  
 
4. If the remedies made available by paragraphs 9 or 12 are imp lemented that 
cause implementation of Section 1.G., Carrier A may also be required to be 
merged with and into NAC. In such event, this LOA will remain in force, and 
the operations of Carrier A and NAC will be fenced, pending completion of the 
procedures of  Section 1.G. of the CBA. Upon completion of Section 1.G 
procedures, this LOA shall become null and void unless otherwise agreed to 
by the parties.    
 
5. Carrier A shall not operate any jet aircraft. Carrier A shall not operate turboprop 
aircraft in cargo ope rations with a maximum payload capacity in excess of 
7,500 pounds, except the following two aircraft [INSERT REG. NUMBERS] 
may carry up to a maximum of 7,500 pounds of cargo.  
  
6. Carrier A shall not acquire or establish another air carrier.  
 
7. Carrier A shall conduct all operations solely under Part 135 or Part 91.  
 
8. Consistent with Paragraph 7, above, and for the avoidance of doubt, Carrier A 
will not possess, acquire, or be operated in whole or in part under, a Part 121, 
125 or 117 operating certificates .   
 
9. A transfer in whole or part of Carrier A, and any successors thereto, to another 
division, section, business unit, Affiliate or Entity of the corporate parent of 
NAS, or any successor thereto, is strictly prohibited. In the event of such 
prohibited transfe r Carrier A, NAS, NAC and their Affiliates, and any successors 
thereto, remain bound by the terms of this LOA.  In addition to any cease -and-
desist  remedies, which shall apply in the case of a prohibited transfer, and any 
other remedies available to the Un ion in the event of a violation, Carrier A, NAS 
and NAC agree the following remedies apply as a result of a prohibited transfer:  
 

--- PAGE BREAK ---

A. NAS and NAC have joint and several liability for liquidated damages to the 
craft or class of NAC Pilots in an amount equal to $100,000.00 per day from 
the date of the transfer until Carrier A again is wholly owned by NAS; IBT 
shall be wholly responsible for directing NAS and/or NAC how to allocate 
such funds among the Pilots;  
 
B. The following provisions shall be implemented until Carrier A again is wholly 
owned by NAS:  
i. NAC Crewmembers on Furlough, if any, shall be immediately 
recalled to Active Service;  
ii. NAC Crewmembers are not subject to Furlough;  
iii. NAC Crewmembers are not subject to downgrade;  
iv. There shall be no reduction in NAC Crewmember compensation or 
benefits as a direct or an indirect result of the violation; and  
v. The growth of the craft or class of P ilots shall not be slowed as a 
direct or indirect result of the violation. Accordingly, if this 
subparagraph is in effect, Letter of Agreement 01 -004 is 
automatically amended to account for flying performed by Carrier A 
rather than the Pilots covered by th e CBA.  
 
C. At the election of the Union:  
i. the exemption from the CBA in Paragraph 2 of this LOA shall cease 
to apply to Carrier A;  
ii. the Union and the Company shall initiate and exhaust the procedures 
set forth in Paragraph 6(f) of Letter of Agreement #7; and/ or  
iii. it may terminate this LOA upon notice written notice to NAS and 
NAC; however, paragraph A and B of this Paragraph 9 would remain 
in effect until Carrier A is again wholly owned by NAS. In addition, 
the NAS, NAC and Carrier A would remain liable to the NAC Pilots 
for any payments and damages under any other part of this LOA that 
accrued prior to termination.  
 
10. NAC and NAS shall submit, and NAS shall require Carrier A to submit, to the 
jurisdiction of the System Board of Adjustment to resolve any dispute r elated 
to the interpretation or application of this LOA.  Carrier A’s submission to the 
jurisdiction of the System Board pursuant to this LOA shall not be or be deemed 
to be evidence that:  
 
A. NAC and Carrier A are a “Single Carrier”;  
 
B. Carrier A is required to treat with IBT beyond the scope of its submission to 
the System Board; or  
 
C. Carrier A is subject, or not, to the Railway Labor Act.  
 
11. This LOA continues to apply if NAS owns or controls any portion of Carrier A.  
NAS agrees the requirement of this paragraph shall be an irrevocable and 

--- PAGE BREAK ---

material condition of any future transaction that results in NAS maintaining any 
ownership or control of any portion of Carrier A.  
 
12. In addition to any cease  and desist  remedies,  which shall apply in the case of 
violat ions referred to in this Paragraph , and any other remedies available to the 
Union,  the parties further agree that if Carrier A violates Paragraphs 5, 6, 7, 8, 
or 11 of this LOA the following remedies shall also apply:  
 
A. NAS and NAC would have joint and seve ral liability for liquidated damages 
to the craft or class of NAC Pilots in an amount equal to $100,000.00 per 
day from the date of the violation until compliance has been established; in 
the event of such a remedy, IBT shall be wholly responsible for dire cting 
NAS and/or NAC how to allocate such funds among the Pilots;  
 
B. The following provisions shall be implemented until the subject violation 
ends:  
i. NAC Crewmembers on Furlough, if any, shall be immediately 
recalled to Active Service;  
ii. NAC Crewmembers are not subject to Furlough;  
iii. NAC Crewmembers are not subject to downgrade;  
iv. There shall be no reduction in NAC Crewmember compensation or 
benefits as a direct or an indirect result violation; and  
v. The growth of the craft or class of Pilots s hall not be slowed as a 
direct or indirect result of the violation. Accordingly, if this 
subparagraph is in effect, Letter of Agreement 01 -004 is 
automatically amended to account for flying performed by Carrier A 
rather than the Pilots covered by the CBA.  
 
C. At the election of the Union:  
i. the exemption from the CBA in Paragraph 2 of this LOA shall cease 
to apply to Carrier A; and/or  
ii. the Union and the Company shall initiate and exhaust the procedures 
set forth in Paragraph 6(f) of Letter of Agreement #7.  
 
13. In the event NAS, NAC and/or Carrier A violates Paragraphs 5, 6, 7, 8, 9, 10, 
11, and/or 12, the parties agree the Union shall be irreparably harmed. 
Therefore, the parties agree the Union shall be entitled to injunctive relief 
restraining NAS, NAC and/or Car rier A for violations of Paragraphs 5, 6, 7, 8, 
9, 10, 11 and/or 12, but such relief shall not be the exclusive remedy. The 
parties also agree the Union shall be entitled to injunctive relief to require the 
performance of the obligations of Paragraphs 5, 6 , 7, 8, 9, 10, 11 and/or 12.  
 
14. There shall be no constraints on Carrier A’s passenger flying under Part 135.  
 
15. Operations under this LOA by Carrier A shall not directly or indirectly: (1) cause 
the Furlough or prevent the Recall of Pilots; (2) reduce the com pensation or 

--- PAGE BREAK ---

benefits of Pilots; (3) reduce the number of Pilots in any Position; or (4) slow 
the growth of the craft or class of Pilots.  
 
16. NAC shall not subcontract, consign, convey, transfer, assign or divert flying to 
Carrier A, and Carrier A shall not o therwise perform flying that NAC could 
perform, if doing so directly or indirectly causes the reduction of revenue flying 
conducted by NAC.  
 
A. Revenue flying conducted by NAC for purposes of this LOA shall be 
measured based on Block Time PCH within the indi vidual geographic 
marketplaces (e.g. within a specific state; between states; or to, from 
and/or within other geographic areas served (e.g., the Caribbean)) 
within which NAC and Carrier A both operate. In accordance with the 
foregoing, Carrier A operations  within an individual geographic 
marketplace in which NAC operates shall not directly or directly cause a 
reduction of NAC Block Time PCH within that individual geographic 
marketplace.  
 
B. NAC Block Time PCH shall be measured monthly based on the monthly 
average over a three -month  period as compared to the monthly average 
over the same three -month  period during the preceding three years.    
a. For example, to assess in December if there has been a loss of 
Block Time PCH during the months of September -November 
2022, the average Block Time PCH for September -November 
2022 would be compared to the average Block Time PCH for 
September -November 2019, 2020 and 2021.  
 
C. Without limiting the application of this paragraph 16, the Parties agree 
that nothing in this LOA shall prohibit Carrier A from continuing to 
perform the flying it is performing on the date the parties reached a 
tentative agreement on this LOA, and doing so does not violate this LOA.  
 
D. Carrier A’s passenger flying under Part 135, and operations under Part 
91, are excluded from this Paragraph 15.  
 
E. In the case of a proven violation, an arbitrator shall order that NAC shall 
cease and desist from continuing the violation, and/or Carrier A shall 
cease and desist continuing the violation, and NAC shall make payment 
to pilots equal to the loss of Block Time PCH compensation (separately 
calculated based on average Captain and First Officer rates for pilots 
Domiciled in the affected geographic marketplace and aircraft type) 
during which the proven violation occu rred, and restore the reduced 
flying caused directly or indirectly by Carrier A conducting the flying, in 
addition to any other appropriate remedy.  In the event of such a 
monetary remedy, IBT shall be wholly responsible for directing NAS 
and/or NAC how to allocate such funds among the Pilots.  

--- PAGE BREAK ---

a. If NAC claims the reduced flying cannot be restored to NAC as a 
result of customer requirements or because the flying no longer 
exists in the NAC system, the burden is on NAC to prove such 
claim.  The Company shall pro vide information to the Union in 
support of such a claim in accordance with Paragraph 17.  
 
17. The Union shall be provided on a monthly basis information regarding NAC and 
Carrier A’s operations, including operational and flight data, necessary to audit 
and de termine compliance with this LOA. NAC or NAS shall provide the 
information to the Union no later than the fifteenth day of the month. The 
Company may require recipients of data pursuant to this paragraph to execute 
appropriate non -disclosure agreements. Th e information to be produced to the 
Union is as follows:  
 
A. All NAC flight segments in the geographic marketplace(s) in which 
Carrier A operates for the preceding month, including aircraft type, tail 
number, city pairs, and Block Time PCH. The information shall be 
provided to the Union in Excel format on an individ ualized and aggregate 
basis.  
 
B. All Carrier A flight segments for the preceding month, including aircraft 
type, tail number, city pairs, block time, and pounds of cargo per 
segment.  
 
C. If NAC claims in response to a grievance that certain flying referred to i n 
Paragraph 16(A) could not be performed by NAC (e.g., due to equipment 
type, regulations, or customer requirements (but not because Carrier A 
can perform the flying more economically)), the burden shall be on NAC 
to prove the flying could not have been pe rformed by NAC. NAC shall 
provide the Union with all documents and information it relies upon or 
considers relevant to its claim (e.g., RFPs and relevant 
correspondence).  “Information” as used in this paragraph shall not 
include any documents or other inf ormation that is attorney/client 
privileged. NAS, NAC and/or Carrier A shall not enter into agreements 
with customers regarding “customer requirements” and/or structure its 
business relationships with customers with an intent to evade, or 
purpose of evadin g, monetary payments to NAC Pilots under Paragraph 
16.   
 
18. If NAS or NAC fails to provide the Union with information required under 
Paragraph 17 by the date it is due or any mutually agreeable extension thereto, 
the remedies shall be as follows, in addition  to any other remedies available to 
the Union:  
 
A. First proven violation: cease and desist and provide the information; and  
 

--- PAGE BREAK ---

B. Second and any subsequent proven violation: cease and desist, provide the 
information, and, if the refusal was not reasonably justified, reimburse the 
Union for costs and expenses associated with enforcing its right to the 
information under Paragraph 18 of the LOA.  
 
19. By signing this LOA, NAS agrees that Carrier A is bound by the terms of this 
LOA. Further, with respect to Carrier A’s obligations under this LOA, NAS 
agrees NAS and NAC are jointly and severally liable for any and all violations 
of such obligations.  
 
20. Duration  
 
Subject to paragraphs 3, 4 and 9, this LOA shall become effective upon 
consummation of the acquis ition of Carrier A, and shall remain in force 
contemporaneously with the CBA or until Carrier A is sold or otherwise 
transferred to another entity that is not an Affiliate of NAS or of the parent of 
NAS; provided, however, if Carrier A is sold, conveyed or  otherwise transferred 
to an Entity to which NAS and/or NAC is sold conveyed or otherwise transferred 
within the meaning of Section 1.F of the CBA, regardless of the structure of the 
transaction, then NAS and/or NAC will require the Entity, as an irrevocab le and 
material condition of the transaction, to assume this LOA in its entirety and 
assume all of  the obligations of NAS and/or NAC and Carrier A’s obligations 
under the this LOA.  
 
21.  A Grievance alleging a violation of this LOA is subject to the expedite d 
procedures in Section 1. H of the CBA.

LETTER OF  AGREEMENT  # 16 
 
By and Between  
 
NORTHERN AIR CARGO, LLC

This Letter of Agreement (“LOA”) is made and entered into by and between Northern 
Aviation Services, LLC (“NAS” or the “Parent”), its successors and assigns, Northern Air 
Cargo (“NAC” or the “Company”), its successors and assigns, and the Pilots in the 
services of NAC as represented by the International Brotherhood of Teamsters, Airline 
Division (collectively, the “Parties”).   
 
WHEREAS, the Parties engaged in good faith negotiations over a crew management 
software project;  
 
THERFORE, BE IT RESOLVED:  
 
1. The Company shall launch a crew management software project team, including 
Union members, and hold its first meeting, within 30 days from the date of 
ratification of the LOA. The purpose of the project team is to work cooperatively to 
improve crew plannin g and scheduling for the benefit of Pilots and the Company. 
The Company shall dedicate resources including a full -time project manager, ITS 
personnel and Subject Matter Experts in order to progress this project as efficiently 
and effectively as possible. T he project team shall work together to review software 
programs utilized by other carriers. The project team, including Union members, 
will give input on requirements and score the ability of potential systems against 
those requirements. Within 6 months th ereafter, the project team shall have agreed 
to requirements and scope of work of, and issued, the RFP, which is consistent 
with Company technology acquisition standards, including cyber security, and 
project management guidelines. The project team shall c ooperate to ensure the 
new program is implemented in a timely and efficient manner.   
 
2.  This LOA is enforceable under Section 19 and Section 20 of the CBA.

3. This LOA shall run concurrently with the CBA.

--- PAGE BREAK ---

Explanation of 
Proposed Letter of Agreement 
Re: Acquisition of Part 135 
Air Carrier 
A Presentation for Teamsters Pilots in the Service of Northern Air Cargo
Note: This document is intended for summary purposes only. The terms of the proposed LOA and 
other negotiated provisions in the ratification packet control for all purposes. 

--- PAGE BREAK ---

BACKGROUND
•NAS/NAC informed Union of a potential acquisition of a Part 135 air 
carrier.
•Negotiations between NAC/NAS and the air carrier are ongoing and 
subject to industry standard non -disclosure agreements until the 
transaction is completed.  As a result, the air carrier is referred to as 
“Carrier A” in the LOA and this presentation. The name will become 
public if transaction is finalized.
•Your EXCO and Teamsters Airline Division representatives received 
and reviewed requested information from NAS/NAC about Carrier A 
and engaged in extensive negotiations over the proposed LOA.

--- PAGE BREAK ---

OUR APPROACH 
•When management wants to discuss a matter that impacts Teamsters 
represented pilots, your Union engages management to protect and 
advance the best interests of the pilot group 
•While the acquisition involves a Part 135 carrier, not a Part 121 
carrier, the Union sought to limit risk and exposure to Teamsters 
represented pilots 
•With risks limited by the LOA, there is the possibility of Teamsters 
represented pilots sharing in the potential upside of the transaction, 
to include growth opportunities from improvements to the NAC 
network and increased revenues to support current pay, benefits and 
working conditions and future improvements

--- PAGE BREAK ---

EXCO RECOMMENDS THE MEMBERS 
RATIFY THE LOA 
•Good faith discussions led to the proposed LOA
•The proposed LOA will not take effect unless the Union membership 
ratifies it by a secret vote
•If the proposed LOA is ratified, it will govern the relationship between 
NAS/NAC and Carrier A and restrict Carrier A operations as described 
in the LOA
•If the proposed LOA is rejected, management may still acquire Carrier 
A.  The acquisition would be subject to the terms of the CBA and 
related letters of agreement, including the possibility that Saltchuk 
would place Carrier A outside of NAS control and operate it without 
the restrictions set forth in the LOA 

--- PAGE BREAK ---

The Status of Carrier A
•Under the proposed LOA, Carrier A is an Affiliate of NAS
•Carrier A and its Pilots are exempted from the CBA if NAS, 
NAC and Carrier A satisfy certain restrictions set forth in the 
proposed LOA
•If NAS, NAC and/or Carrier A violate the specified restrictions 
in the proposed LOA, the LOA contains agreed upon 
remedies, including but not limited to the loss of the 
exemption from the CBA. 

--- PAGE BREAK ---

Negotiated Restrictions on Carrier A 
•Carrier A currently conducts cargo and passenger operations under 
Part 135
•The LOA prohibits Carrier A from operating under or acquiring a Part 
121 certificate or conducting operations other than under Part 135
•The LOA prohibits Carrier A from operating aircraft with a maximum 
payload capacity of 7,500 lbs.  The LOA grandfathers two specific 
aircraft currently operated by Carrier A, which may carry up to a 
maximum of 7,500 lbs. of cargo.
•LOA prohibits Carrier A from acquiring or establishing another air 
carrier.

--- PAGE BREAK ---

Agreed Upon Remedies for Violations 
•If Carrier A violates these restrictions (or if Carrier A is moved by 
Saltchuk to another division (not NAS) after the acquisition), the 
LOA provides for multiple agreed upon remedies including:
•Injunctive relief 
•Cease and desist 
•Liquidated damages of $100,000.00 per day
•Recalls and prohibition on furloughs, downgrades, loss of 
compensation and slowing of the growth of the Pilot group
•Loss of CBA exemption
•Union triggered negotiations over amendments to the CBA 
with a requirement that both sides will request a 
proffer/release from mediation 

--- PAGE BREAK ---

Pay Protections Under the LOA
•Carrier A operations are not restricted geographically
•However, NAC cannot subcontract, consign, convey, transfer, assign or divert flying to 
Carrier A, and Carrier A shall not otherwise perform flying that NAC could perform, if 
doing so directly or indirectly causes a reduction of revenue flying conducted by NAC.
•A loss of revenue flying is determined by the amount of Block Time PCH paid to pilots 
operating in the specific geographic market.
•NAC must make payments to pilots equal to the loss of Block Time PCH compensation 
(separately calculated based on average Captain and First Officer rates for pilots 
Domiciled in the affected geographic marketplace and aircraft type) during which the 
proven violation occurred, and restore the reduced flying caused directly or indirectly by 
Carrier A conducting the flying, in addition to any other appropriate remedy.
•If NAC claims the reduced flying cannot be restored to NAC as a result of customer 
requirements or because the flying no longer exists in the NAC system, the burden is on 
NAC to prove the claim.  The Company must provide information to the Union in support 
of such a claim.

Information

and
•Second and any subsequent proven violation :cease and desist,
provide the information, and, ifthe refusal was not reasonably
justified, reimburse theUnion forcosts and expenses associated with
enforcing itsright totheinformation under Paragraph 18oftheLOA.

--- PAGE BREAK ---

Other Protections
•The LOA becomes part of the CBA and is fully enforceable through 
expedited arbitration and court proceedings
•While Carrier A is not being integrated with NAC at this time, certain 
violations of the LOA will trigger a loss of the exemption from the CBA 
and integration of Carrier A with NAC at the election of the Union 
and/or opening up our CBA for amendments
•If NAC and/or NAS are not sold in the future, but Carrier A is sold to 
Entity not affiliated with NAS or Saltchuk, the LOA no longer applies
•If NAC and/or NAS are sold in the future, and the same Entity acquires 
Carrier A, then the acquiring Entity must assume the LOA, including 
the restrictions on Carrier A, as a condition of the sale

•The ratification packet include 3 new, unrelated improvements that take 
effect if the LOA is ratified:
•In response to OE delay, Pilots will receive the higher rate of pay starting on the 
101st day after training begins or the date OE commences, whichever occur first 
(subject to limited exceptions due to circumstances beyond the control of the 
Company and/or Pilot absence (in which case the 101 day provision is adjusted on a 
day-for-day basis)
•If a Pilot does not begin OE within 100 Days after training begins, the two (2) year 
Aircraft Freeze shall be reduced by every Day in excess of 100 Days (subject to 
limited exceptions for circumstances beyond the control of the Company and/or Pilot 
absence (in which case the 100 day provision is adjusted on a day -for-day basis))
•A Company -Union crew management software team starts work within 30 days after 
ratification of the LOA and must issue RFPs within 6 months thereafter

MOU #1 : PTO Day Conversion and Redistribution Process.  
Dear Mr. Macri : 
This letter  will confi rm our mutual understan ding and a greement regarding  the 
intended application of the new PTO and Vacation provisions in this Agreement, 
including, but not l imited to , the assurance that a  Pilot shall have the  availability to use  
his accrued PTO Days from his PTO Bank  when taking his scheduled Vacation. To 
assure that a Pilot shall have  access to  one h undred percent  100% of his  accrued 
PTO for  use in the following Year, the following processes shall be implemented: (a) 
If a Pilot ’s PTO Bank  reaches the maximum accrual limit of thirty (30)  PTO Days 
before  December 31st of that Year,  all additional PTO Da ys that the Pilot accrues in 
that Year shall continue to be  deposited into his PTO Bank (“Annual PTO Overages”). 
(b) On December 31st  of each Year, the Company shall convert all  Annual PTO
Overages from each affected  Pilot’s PTO Bank  to Sick Leave Days and then
redeposit  each Pilot’s  new Sick Leave Days into  their respective  Sick Leave Bank
(“SLB”), as provided in Section 10 (Sick Leave). (c) During this annual redis tribution
process, only  those Pilots who  have  accrued  more than  thirty ( 30) PTO Days in his
PTO Bank  shall be subject to this redistribution process . This redistribution process
shall cease as soon as a Pilot’s PTO Bank balance reaches the maximum accrual
limit and he  shall begin the new Year with thirty (30) PTO Days in his P TO Bank, (d)
A Pilot shall not participate in this conversion or redistributio n processes if his PTO
Bank balance is not over the maximum accrual limit on December 31st of that Year,
(e)Unless otherwise provided for in this Agreement, a Pilot sh all be lim ited to the use
of thirty (30) PTO Days from his PTO Bank . (f) a Pilot who sep arates from the
Company shall be paid for all his accrued PTO Days in his PTO Bank, up to a
maximum of thirty (30) Days, at his Hourly Pay Rate, as provided in Section 3
(Compens ation), at the time of his separation.
At the time of the signing of this MO U, there  may have been Pilots who have had their 
PTO Days  converted into Sick Days and redeposited into their Sick Leave Bank prior 
to December 31st of this Year . The Company agrees that upon the signing of this 
MOU, they sha ll by re-depositing one hundred percent (100%) of those converted 
PTO Days  back into the ir respective  PTO Bank . 
The Company and the Union mutually agree to adopt the above -mentioned processes 
in order to  assur e that a Pilot  shall have the    ability to fully utilize his  PTO Day  
accruals.     
Please  indicate  your accep tance by signin g below.  DocuSign Envelope ID: 7A46D395-CB86-4F80-B6A9-EE3300CB9708

MOU #2 : Positive Contac t Responsibilit ies. 
Dear Mr. Macri : 
This letter  will confi rm our mutual understan ding and a greement regarding  the proper 
application of subsections 13.H. and 15.D. when  changes to a Pilot’s schedule is 
changed, including the notification of a Reserve Pilot’s RAP and Rest Period Times . 
Each Pilot is required to provide their primary contact telephone number to the  
Company , including any changes or updates . Unless otherwise mutually agreed upon 
by the Pilot and Crew Scheduling , this telephone number shall  be the only means of 
creating  “Positive C ontact ” with a Pilot  when Crew Scheduling changes a Pilot’s  
scheduled Assignment (s) in his Line . When  a Pilot’s  primary contact telephone 
number becomes  unusable, it shall be his responsi bility to inform the C rew scheduling, 
prior to his next scheduled Assignment, of his alternate contact method. The Pilot may, 
at his sole discretion, provide the Company with alternate contact numbers and/or 
emails that m ay be used, but unless the Pilot no tifies the Company of a change in his 
primary contact number or email address, the Company shall only be obligated to 
utilize the previous primary contact method that the Pilot  has authorized. As a courtesy 
after making Positive Contact with the Pilot, the  Company may follow up the call with 
an email that covers the content of their conversation. In the event a telephone number 
cannot be used to make  Positive Contact with a  Pilot, alternate means may be mutually 
arranged between the Pilot and Crew Scheduling, such as the  use of an email address 
or another approved PCD , in order  to assure that  Positive Contact  is made . 
The Company and the Union mutually agree to adopt the above -mentioned processes 
to assure that Positive Contact between the Pilot and the Company is accomplished.

MOU #4 : Reassignment to a new  type of Reserve Assignment.  
Dear Mr. Macri : 
This letter  will confi rm our mutual understan ding and a greement regarding  a Pilot 
who is  Reassigned  to another type of Reserve Assignment when  already  
schedul ed to a Reserve Assignment  in his Line . As provided in 14.J Reassignment, 
the Collective Bargaining  Agree ment (CBA) provides limitations and restrictions to 
Reassigning a Pilot who is scheduled to pe rform a  Trip Pairing  in his Line. The 
parties agree that it is the intent ion of  subsection 14.J., to prohibit Crew 
Scheduling from Reassigning a  Pilot who is performing or is  scheduled to 
perform  a Trip Pairing  to a Reserve Assignment. Furthermore, it is also agree d 
that the intent of this subsection is to prohibit Crew Scheduling from Reassigning a 
Pilot who  “is performing ” any Assignment to a Reserve Assignment, except  when 
Reassigned to  a R1 or R2 Reserve Availability Period (RAP)  and is  Reassigned  to 
a R4 RAP.  The parties also agreed that it was not the intent  to prohibit Crew 
Scheduling from  Reassigning a Pilot  who has a  scheduled  Reserve Assignment  in 
his Line , to another Type of Reserve Assignment, so long as it is not during the 
same Duty Perio d and it must and must be  on the same  scheduled  Day(s)  as his 
previously scheduled Reserve Assignments . When a Pilot , who is currently 
performing  a Reserve Assignment , is notified that he is to be  Reassign ed in the 
future  to another type of Reserve Assignment , he must be provided applicable 
Rest prior to beginning his new Reserve Assignment.   
In Subsection 3.F., Reserve Pay provides  the direction  as to how a Pilot  with a  
scheduled Reserve Assignment  in his Line is paid when he is subsequently 
assig ned to  perform “a Trip Pairing ” or “other Company -Directed Assignment s.” 
Section 2, Definitions provides a clear understanding of the definitions for 
“Company -Directed Assignments ” and “Assignments” . Under the definition of an 
Assignment, it references an example  of an Assignment  as a “Reserve Period.”  
Subsection ’s 14.J.5.a. and 14.J.5.b. also references specific instances when a Pilot 
who is scheduled to perform a Reserve Assignment may be Reassigned back into 
a previously scheduled  Reserv e Assignment. In this in stance, the  parties  intended 
that a  Reassignment  from a scheduled Reserve Assignment to another type of 
Reserve Assignment was legal, subject to  the provision’s stated  restrictions and 
limitations .  
When Crew Scheduling  Reassigns a Pilot to another  type  of Reserve Assignment, 
the following Restrictions and Limitations shall apply.    
(1) W hen Reassigning a Pilot to  R1 RAP’s, Crew Scheduling  shall immediately
schedul e the Pilot  for one (1) Day Off in every seven (7) Days  in his Line and provide
him with t he applicable DOT’s and Duty Off Times for each  within each new R1 RAP.
(2) A Pilot who is Reassigned to a new type of Reserve Assignment shall be
scheduled to perform that new type of Reserve Assignment on the same Days as his
originally scheduled Reserve Assignments in his Line.DocuSign Envelope ID: 7A46D395-CB86-4F80-B6A9-EE3300CB9708
Page 322 of 333

--- PAGE BREAK ---

(3)If Crew Scheduling intends to  notify a Pilo t who is performing or is scheduled to
perform a RAP  that he is to be Reassigned to another Type of Re serve
Assignment  in the future  and there are more than two Pilots who are avail able for
such Reassignment , they shall Reassign the Pilot utilizing the First -In/First -Out
(FIFO) provisions, as provided in Section 15 (Reserve) , and
(4)(4) As provided in 14.E. 12., Minimum Net Reserve Compliment, Crew Planning
shall, to the extent possible, construct in each Domicile a minimum number of
Reserve Lines that contain R1 RAP’s to cover each  Day in the Month.
(5)A Pilot who has R1 RAP’s  in his Line  shall not have them  Reassigned to another  type
of Reserve Assignments.
(6)A Pilot assigned to  a R2 RAP(s) or R3 Reserve Assignment (s), he may be reassigned
a R1  RAP(s) . When  Reassig ned, Crew Scheduling shall  first make “Positive Contact”
with the affected Pilot .
(7)When the Reassignment  in paragraph (6)  involves an R2  to an R1 RAP  and Crew
Schedulin g provides the Pilot with  at least  a forty-eight (48)  hour notice  in advance of
the DOT of his first scheduled R1 RAP, the Pilot shall  be responsible for his own Travel
to his Domicile . When the notification for such Reassignment is less than  forty-eight
(48)hours, the Company shall  then provide him Deadhead Travel  to his Domicile.
(8)When the Reassignment in paragraph (6) involves  a R3  Reserve Assignment(s)  to
an R1 RAP(s)  or R3 Reserve Assignments to an  R2 RAPs , the Pilot shall be provided
at least a twelve  (12) hour notice  before required to Report for Duty .
(9)When a Pilot is located in an Out -of-Domicile Location performing or scheduled to
perform a block of R2 RAP’s and he is assigned to a Trip Pairing that includes
Deadhead/Flight Segments into his Domicile and scheduled R1 RAP’s, Crew
Scheduling shall  provide him with a hotel room, per Diem and his Trip Rig shall
continue throughout his time in Domicile when such Trip Pairing contains two (2)
or fewer consecutive R1 RAP’s and/or 2 Days of Flight Segments . When, under
the same conditions the Trip Pairing is scheduled with three (3) or more
consecutive R1 RAP’s and/or Flight Segments, the Trip Rig for that Trip Pairing
shall end upon arriving in Domicile and a new Trip Rig will not begin until he is
assigne d to his next Trip Pairing  If the Pilot is initially scheduled to a  Tr ip Pairing
is scheduled to three or more consecutive R1 RAP’s in Domicile, but is then
Reassigned to a Trip Pairing with a only two (2) consecutive R1 RAP’s and/or
flight Segments, his  original Trip Rig shall restart as if it never stopped.
(10) When a Pilo t is located at an Out -of-Domicile location and is performing or
scheduled to perform an R2 RAP and is Reassigned to perform a future R3
Reserve Assignment(s), Crew Scheduling shall provide him with Deadhead Travel
back to his Residence Airport.
(11) When a P ilot has not  been Deadheaded or he has not flown a Flight Segment
to an Out -of-Domicile location to perform a scheduled R2 RAP(s) and Crew
Scheduling then assigns him to a R3 Reserve Assignment(s), the Company shall
not be responsible to provide any Deadhead Travel, paid Hotel accommodations,
or Per Diem, while traveling to or performing his new Reserve Assignment.
(12) When it involves a Reassignment of a R3 Reserve Assignment to a  R1 RAP, the
Reassignment shall be at least  three (3)  consecutive  Days  of R1 RAP’s . In the event
Crew Scheduling realizes that they do not need the Pilot for the entire three (3) Days,
the Pilot may request to be Reassigned back to his originally scheduled  R3 Reserve
Assignment.DocuSign Envelope ID: 7A46D395-CB86-4F80-B6A9-EE3300CB9708

First-In/First -Out (FIFO) provisions, as provided in Section 15 (Reserve). When it is
prior to the beginning of the Month and that Month’s applicable FIFO List , they shall
Reassign the more junior Pilot  first.

MOU #5: Pay Implications  to Lines  during the Monthly Bid Process . 
Dear Mr. Macri : 
This letter  will confi rm our mutual understan ding and a greement regardin g pay 
applications as it relates to a Pilot’s  Line PCH value and how any additional PCH he earns 
in the Month is applied to the MPG  (65 PCH), as provided in subsection 3.D . Under 
Subsection 3.N. (Month ly Cumulative PCH), it assumes  that each Line  at the beg inning 
of each Month  has a PCH value at or above the MPG .  As provided  in 14.E.7., “All Lines 
shall be valued at no less than MPG, as provided in Section 3 (Compensation), and 
constructed to no more than ninety -five (95) PC H.” Except as provided elsewhere  in this 
Agreement , it is understood  that all Regular, Composite and Reserve  Lines that are 
constructed by the Company  shall have a PCH value or above the MPG  (65 PCH) . 
Further more, if  the Company con structs a Line that has an actual PCH value that is less 
than the MPG, that Line shall have a published  Initial  Line PCH value o f 65 PCH  and any 
PCH increases or decreases  resulting from the Monthly Integration procedures, as 
provided in subsection 14.E., shall be applied to a Line’s actual PCH value it is higher 
than the MPG and 65 PCH, when a  Line has a PCH value that is equal to, or less than 
the MPG.    
As understood in the paragraph above, a Regular Line may realize a decrease in its Initial 
Line PCH value during the Integration Procedures. As provided  in 14.G., it also states 
that a  Pilot who is awarded a Regular  Line may participate in SAP. When a Regular 
Line’s  PCH value falls below the MPG,  as a result of the application of  one or more of the 
Month ly Integration Procedures, a Pilot  shall initiate SA P with “super -seniority” status  for 
the purpose of recovering his Line PCH  back  to the MPG . Once his Regular  Line value 
has been  recovered, he shall revert to his proper Seniority status in his Fleet Type  and 
Domicile and may continue to participate in SA P. If after SAP,  a Pilot does  not participate  
to the extent necessary in order to  recover his  Regular  Line PCH  back to the MPG , 
subsection 14.G.4. directs  the Company to assign available Trip Pairings from Open Time 
and/or Reserve Assignme nts (in Open Time or not)  to any Days Off  on his  Regular  Line 
that were  original  Workdays on  his Initial Line award . Once the MPG has been reached, 
the Company shall cease to add additional Trip Pairings and/or Reserve Ass ignments . 
If, as provided in this  paragraph, the Company is unable recover a Pilot’s  Regular  Line 
PCH to the MPG, the parties agree that his individual MPG for the Month shall be adjusted 
to the PCH value o n his Final Line Award  and all additional PCH tha t is earned in the 
Month shall be in addition to that adjusted MPG value.  
The parties agree that it is important to have  an effective  SAP process. Therefore, the 
Company agrees, prior to constructing the Initial Lines,  to follow  the Monthly  PCH “hold -
back” parameters  in each Domicile  for each Fleet Type:  
(1)Three hundred ( 300) PCH  or less , the allowable maximum of fifteen  percent (15%) .
(2)More than  three hundred (300) and five hundred (500) PCH – holdback of at least
twelve (12%) perc ent.
(3) Mor e than five hundred (500) PCH and six Hundred (600) PCH – at least nine percent
(9%) holdback.DocuSign Envelope ID: 7A46D395-CB86-4F80-B6A9-EE3300CB9708
Page 325 of 333

--- PAGE BREAK ---

(4) More than six hundred (600) PCH and seven hundred (700) PCH – at least seven
percent (7%) holdback.
(5)More than seven Hundred (700) PCH and nine hundred ( 900) PCH – at least six
percent (6%)  holdback.
(6)More than eight hundred (800) PCH and one thousand (1000) PCH – at least five
percent (5%) holdback.
(7)More than one thousand (1000) and one thousand -two hundred (1200) PCH – at least
4 percent (4% ).
(8)Above one  thousand -two hundred (1200) PCH – the minimum of three percent (3%)
As provided in this Agreement, the parties agree  that a Pilot who has been  assigned or 
awarded  a Composite and  Reserve Line  cannot participate in SAP. As a result of this 
restriction, a ll Composite and Reserve Lines after the Final Bid Award shall have a PCH 
value at or above  the MPG  and all additional PCH earned in the Month shall be paid in 
addition to the MPG , except , when  a Pilo t is awarded or assigned to a Reserve or 
Composite Line a nd he  utilizes his awarded Vacation in a Month, but does not have the 
required number of PTO Days in his PTO Bank  in order  to cover the PCH  requirements 
inside his Vacation Block , he shall  utilize hi s remaining  PTO Days  from his PTO Bank 
and if his Line PC H falls below sixty -five PCH (MPG), his Line MPG shall be adjusted  to 
his Final Bid Line PCH and all additional earned PCH in the Month shall be paid in addition 
to that adjusted MPG .   
When the Scheduling Committee agrees to utilize the Secondary Bid Pro cess in a 
Domicile, as provided in subsection 14.H.1., and after the Integration Process  a Pilot’s 
Line PCH falls below the MPG, the Company  shall utilize the available provisions , as 
provided in subsection 14.H. to recover his PCH up to the MPG. In all cases under the 
Secondary Bid Process, since a Pilot is unable to utilize the SAP Process, his  MPG shall 
be 65 PCH, as provided in subsection 3.D.,  and all additional PCH that is earned in the 
Month shall be in addition to his MPG.  
It is understood by the  parties that  such provisions in Section 14 is intended to give the 
Pilot and the Company the ability to recover a Pilot’s Line PCH up to the MPG. It is also 
understood that the Company may elect to build Lines that are less than the MPG, but 
subsection 14.E.7. protects such Line value to the MPG. I f, after the SAP Process or 
after the Secondary Bid Process , the Company elects not to utilize the  available  
provisions  in Section 14 to recover a Pilot’s Line PCH  to the MPG ,  this inaction  by the 
Company  shall not negatively affect the Pilot’s Line value  and the Line PCH shall begin 
the Month at the MPG, so long as no other further actions are taken by the Pilot that 
would increase or decrease his Line PCH, as provided for in this Agreement.    
This MOU shall no t circumvent or become an alternative to the Grievance or System 
Board of Adjustment processes, as provided in Sections 19 and 20, but is intended to  
be used for the purpose of potentially remedying any submitted grievance by a Pilot(s) 
or the EXCO.

MOU # 6: Company Paid Move Entitlements. 
Dear Mr. Macri : 
This letter  will confi rm our mutual understan ding and a greement regarding  the 
timeliness of a Company Paid Move . Once  a Pilot is awarded a Vacancy , as 
provided in  Subsection 6.F.2.  and completes his Training for the awarded Vacancy 
and/or assumes his Vacancy in a different Domicile, he shall qualify for a Company 
Paid Move, when he meets the requirements in subsection 6.F .2.  
Subsection 18.F. provid es the Company to notify the Pilo ts with  a minimum amount 
of information  for each Vacancy  or Displacement  Bid. One requirement is to provide 
an Effective Date for each  Vacancy  or Displacement in each Bid. In the definition of 
an “Effective Date, ” as provid ed in Section 2, Definitions , it states :  “(b) the date on 
which a Vacancy becomes an active Position within the Company and/or Domicile .” 
Furthermore, in subsection 12.A.3., it defines  what is a Training  Event  and OE is 
the final phase of each Training Ev ent. Once his Training Event has been 
successfully completed and he assumes his new Vacancy on its Effective Date or 
afterwards, if a Pilot’s Training has exceeded the published Effective Date, it now  
becomes an “ Active Position” in that Domicile  and at su ch time, he shall qualify for 
his Company Paid Move, including the start of his one (1) year clock.   
When  Training is not required, if a Pilot is awarded a Position in a different 
Domicile,  due to a Vacancy or Displacement Bid,  he shall be  entitled to  a Company 
Paid Move , if he qualifies for such move, as provided in subsection 6.F.2.  At the 
time he assumes his new Position from a new Vacancy or Displacement Award,  i.e., 
the Effective Date of the Vacancy, he shall have one  (1) Year to initi ate his 
Company Paid Move.   
For all Domiciles that were  “New Domicile s” at the DOS of this Agreement, the 
Pilots who were awarded Vacancies in these New Vacancies shall have one (1) 
Year, beginning on  October 1, 2018,  to initiate his Company Paid Move .   
Should  a dispute arise regarding the applicability or definition of any of the 
provisions within this MOU, the EXCO and the Company shall convene  a meeting 
within fourteen (14) Days . Any such discussions shall not circumvent or become an 
alternative to the Grieva nce or System Board of Adjustment processes, as provided 
in Sections 19 and 20, but may be used for the purpose of  successfully resolving 
such dispute or to remedy a  previously submitted grievance by a Pilot(s) or the 
EXCO.

Dear Mr. Macri :
